¶the hiſtory herodian greeke authour treating romayne emperor marcus tranſlated oute greeke latin angelus politianus latin englyſhe nicholas smyth whereunto annexed argumentes euery booke begynnyng thereof annotacions better vnderſtandynge ſame hiſtorye ¶cum gratia priuilegio regali ad imprimendum ſolum vvilliam coplande ❧to ryghte honorable lorde wyllyam earle penbroke c lorde preſident kyng queenes maieſties counſayle march wale one theyr maieſties moſt honorable preuie counſaile humble oratour nycholas smyth wyſheth thynges proſperous amongeſt thoſe haue theyr wrytynge beautifyed greke latyn tonge none ſuppoſed right honorable vertuous lord ſo much haue profited mortall affaire hiſtoriographers haue faythfully reduced writyng actes deades ſuch fame either good euyll haue paſſed thys tranſitorye lyfe haue put eye lyues maners doinges ſortes men wt theyr counſelles fortune aduentures whiche theyr poſteritie maye paynted table beholde therby learne profyte aſwell common wealthe owne priuate eſtate chieflye manyfold example bothe good euyll conteyned hiſtories ſortes people may attayne knowledge ſhorte ſpace otherwyſe might al theyr liues ye ſame much lōger commō age man profe wherof haue memorie lucius lucullus noble romaine cicero wryteth departure frō rome againſt great kyng mythridates beyng vtterly vnſkylfull warfare whyles ſayled sea ſo trauayled conferring wyth learned men reading hiſtories arriued aſie ſo excellente warlyke knowledge confeſſion mythridates deſerued preferment aboue chieuetaynes warre tyme alexander seuerus alſo emperour rome ſo euer made preparation warre accuſtomed conſulte wt ſuch expert hiſtories good cauſe yf vſe ſayeth afranius hath engendred wyſedome memorye moother hath brought lyghte oughte ſage diſcrete whiche reteyne memorie deades maners one age citie al age nacions thys much conſiderynge ryght excellent lorde enduced prudente wordes saluſt hys preface catilines wonderfull coniuration wherby exhorteth man yf entende reputed worthyer mortall creature ſo employe hys whole labour ſtudye ouerſlyp hys lyfe ſlouthful ſilence ſauage brute beaſtes nature hath fourmed prone ſubiect ye filthie luſtes bealy haue enterpryſed trāſlate latyn preſente hiſtorie herodian greke authour treating romayn emperours betwene marcus philoſopher gordianus yonger thynke brought oure englyſhe tonge haue preſumed dedicat ye ſame vnto good lordſhyp whome onely fame alſo experience doeth apparaūtly proue perfect patrone knyghtlye prowes vertue humbly beſechyng good lordſhyp accuſtomed clemencie ſo accepte thys ſymple gift beyng croppe barreyne harueſt may embolden ioyfullye embrace encourage employe poore labour hereafter ſo remayne continuall interceſſor almyghtye god proſperous eſtate youre lordſhyppe wyth contynuall encreaſe vertue honour ¶the proheme hiſtorie herodian treating romayne emperours marcus whiche haue delyuered vnto theyr poſteritie auncient tradicions endeuored renewe writyng olde memorye hyſtories ſaye earneſtly affecting renowne erudicion learning buſyly ſtudyeng preſerue theyr name thiniurie obliuion employ moche leſſe laboure ſearching oute truthe trimmynge ſtyle hiſtories knowinge preciſely althoughe falſefyed thing longe theyr time paſſed ſame coulde reprehendid yet neuertheles ſelfes ſhold pleaſaunt eloquence finely penned talke obtayne muche commoditie paynefull trauayle ſome beyng moued perticuler enmityes hatred tyrauntes elles fallen vnmeaſurable flaterye prayſyng prince cyties priuate perſons dyd ſkylfull knowledge wryting blaſe extoll farre aboue truthe thinges ſelues ſymple eſtimacion contrarie wyſe haue enterpryſed wryte hiſtorye receyued others vnknowen elles wanting witneſſes preſent fixed remaining memory reader collected ſynguler trueth diligence truſtyng knowledge thoſe thinges many great longe agone happened wyll vnpleaſaunt poſterite yf mā wyll well ponder al age ſynce time auguſtus romayne ſuperioritie commytted arbitrement one man ſhall fynde thoſe iic yeres ſo many almoſt perdy reckened betwene auguſtus marcus ſo diuers ſucceſſions thempire ſo variable chaunces happes warres either ciuyle foreyn ſo manie nacions raiſed vp ſo many owne barbarous city deſtroyed beſides earthquake plague liues alſo prince tiraunts ſo ſtraunge incredible none leſt verie like example founde amongs elder whiche prince ſome longe tyme remayned authoritie ſome ſhorte enioyed dominion yea many ſcarcelie entered honour onlie named emperours loſt thempire verie ſame daye tooke vpon ſpace lx yeres citie rome ſuſtained gouernours time ſufficed came paſſe many ſtraunge thinges worthy admiracion chaunced prince ſomewhat ſtriken age men expert ſundry affayres prudently gouerne themſelues charge thother ſide yonge men ledinge liues voluptuouſnes inuented commaunded new thinges dayly wherbie happened yonge prince beinge vnlike age licence alſo folow vnlike ſtudie maners theſe thinges done obſeruinge iuſt order trew tyme prynces declare ¶the contentes fyrſte booke authour beginneth hiſtorye ende marcus antoninus reigne ſucceſſor vnto aurelius antoninus ſurnamed pius behoueth know ye opiniō euſebius table marcus antoninus xiiii emperour rome opinion hiſtoriographers xvii fyrſt iulius ceſar ſeconde octauius ceſar auguſtus thirde tiberius ceſar iiii caius caligula v claudius ceſar vi nero claudius ceſar vii sergius galba viii otho siluius ix aulus vitellius x flauius veſpaſianus xi titus veſpaſianus twelue domitianus whiche twelue suetonius tranquillus hathe wryten compendiouſlye paulus oroſius ſayeth nerua ſucceaded domitian nerua traian traian adrian adrian antoninus pius wyth hys two sonnes aurelius lucius whome marcus antonīus verus aurelius commodus brother ſucceaded marcus antonīus whome preſently queſtion ouerliued remained ſole emperour beyng xvii nombre reckening iulius ceſar fyrſte lignage vertue ſcience deceaſe marcus herodian ſpeaketh begynnynge fyrſte booke whome sonne commodus raigned beyng begynning gentle meeke good diſpoſicion eſcaped treaſon lucilla owne syſter perennes capitayne garde • ternus cleander liuetenaunte armie altered diſſolute diſhoneſt lyfe tirannie wherfore poyſoned martia one cōcubynes letus capitaine hys garde electus principall chāberlaine appoyntment ſtrangled narciſſus finis ¶the fyrſte booke hiſtorie herodian themperour marcus many doughtersthe childerne marcus veriſſimus ii ſonnes onely whome yonger named veriſſimus myſchaunce died tender age named commoduscommodus father broughte vp wt great diligence care hauynge goten partes excellente learned men waged thē large ſtipendes ſhoulde euery man hys parte garnyſſhe maners diſpoſicion hys sonne maryed doughters rype age vnto beſt senatours chooſyng sonnes lawe ſuche coulde ſhew furthe large pedegrues aunceſtrie ſuche vaunted ſelues great treaſoure thoſe excelled perfecte modeſtie maners innocencie lyfe eſteamed onely perfecte ſtable rycheſſe mynde ¶he forgate vertuethe good diſpoſicion marcus wherin exerciſed hym ſelfe beyng ſo ſtudious antiquitie learnyng ſame might compared beſt eyther greekes romaynes profe hereof many thinges bothe ſpoken writen hym commen euen vnto tyme ſo curteis would gentely take euery commer vnto hym hande permytting man ſhoulde forbidden garde approching vnto perſon onely amonges emperours vſed ſtudy sapience woordes knowledge decree grauitie maners continencie lyfe wherby came paſſe ſame age tyme brought furthe great encreaſe wyſe men communely men wont folowe lyues maners prynces touching notable actes hym done aſwell rome elles behaued hym ſelfe alſo towardes barbarous nacions enhabytinge eaſte northe ſame contayned monumentes many excellent learned men thoſe thinges whyche death marcus age bothe ſawe harde whereof many experience ſelfe knewe one traded common affayres prince buſineſſe haue taken vpon wryte pannonie¶whyles olde emperour marcus ſoiourned amōges pannoniens greuous diſeaſe came vpon hym onely worne wyth age alſo ſore broken wyth continuall trauaile care wherfore perceyued remedy death beganne greatly doubte hym ſelfe leſt hys sonne entered fyrſt yeres adoleſcencie eyther throughe vehemencie hys youtheadoleſcencie elles throughe inordynate lycence whyche ſhould haue hys father deathe leuynge good exerciſe ſtudy aparte wold addycte ſelfe dronkenneſſe ſuperfluous ryot knewe well myndes yonge men eaſily declyne immoderate ſuperfluytie laudable honeſt dyſciplyne troubled beſydes wyth memory many prince whiche beyng yonge men tooke vpon gouernaunce royaulmes well dioniſius tiraunt siciledioniſius whoſe intemperatenes lyfe ſo great endowed richeſt rewardes thinuentours newe pleaſures alſo whyche ſucceaded alexander macedonie dyd ſo ſhamefullye tiranouſlye raygne purchaſed hys kyngedome notorious obloquy ptolomeus fell ſo deteſtable lyfeptolomeus contrarye lawes macedoniens greekes entangled thinceſt mariage hys owne syſter antigonus alſoantigonus bacchus repreſent god bacchus wonte ſteade macedonien diademe crowne garlande yuie ſceptre carye thyſtell olde man vexid beſydes wyth late example neronero abſtayned murdering hys owne moother made hym ſelfe laughynge ſtocke vnto people remembred domytiandomitiā lefte nothynge vndone thoughte appertayne vnto extreame crueltye wherefore wayeng wyth hym ſelfe thieſe ymages tyrannye toſſed betwene hope feare nygh nacion germaynes encreaſed alſo hys perplexitie hadde throughly broughte ſubiection ſome taken hys frendſhyppe reſte vanquyſſhed force batayle many ſame eſcaped hydde ſelues feare prynce wherefore doubted greately leaſte hys deathe woulde rebelle agayne ſettynge noughte youthe hys sonne knewe nature barbarous people ſturred wyth euery ſmall tryfle beynge turmented wyth thieſe troubleſome waues care cauſed manye hys friendes kynſmen company repayre vnto preſence theyr commynge togythers hauyng commaunded hys sonne ſtande lyfted hym ſelfe ſomewhat vpon hys pylowe made oracion vnto ¶it meruayled atthe oracion marcus vpon hys death bed ſorowfull penſyfe beholding plighte nature man bewaile miſfortune thoſe thinges ſee eye doo prouoke muche compaſſion pitie beſydes reaſon commune recompence good wyll haue heretofore borne hope duty loke mutuall beneuolence handes preſente ſo happened muſt make profe whether haue vayne ſo longe fore exhybited honour vnto hauing alwayes eſtimacion employed diligent ſtudie towardes welthe recompencing ſame ſhewe ſelues vnmyndefull benefytes haue receyued ye ſee ſon ſelues haue noriſhed entering nowe firſt boundes youthe ſwolowe waues mortall lyfe wāting gouernours leſt ye ignoraunce beyng drawen ryghte courſe acquaynte himſelfe diſordered exercyſes therfore one many father vnto hym garnyſhing maners wyth prompting minyſtring holſome preceptes vnto hym neyther maye aboundaunce treaſour ſatiſfie ſenſual luſtes tyranny neyther emperoure aſſuredly defended bande garde enuyroning hys perſon except haue good willes thoſe gouerneth euermore raigne longe peaceably feare cruelti loue gentlenes powred harte citezyns neyther whome force conſtrayneth thoſe free wylles obey eyther ſuffering exempt frō ſuſpiciō flatery ſame tyme except outragiouſly handeled grudge impugne rule ſuperiours harde man lyueth mooſt inordinate licence gouerne ſelf bridle affection wherfore yf ye wilbe authours well lyuing vnto oftentimes admonyſhe thoſe thinges preſently heareth ye ſhal one labour bothe make hym good prynce vnto ſelfes alſo deſerue participation memorye whiche one poynt ye maye make immortall whyles themperour marcus ſpeaking thieſe wordes vitall ſpirite began ſo ſodeinly fayle furthwyth enforced ceaſe talke ſlyde downe bed agayne ſo greate compaſſion perced heartes preſent many beyng ſorowe almoſt berafte ryght ſenſes rayſed dolorouſe clamour hauyng languyſſhed onely day nyght ended hys lyfe leuing behinde great wante deſyre hym ſelfe vnto men age vnto poſterite perpetuall renowne vertue fame death ſpreadde abroade incredible lamentacion aſwel amongeſt hole armye ſelfe common people man within romaine dominion receiued meſſage without abundaunt ſheading teares bewayleng loſſe wt one accorde ſome called hym good father ſome bening emperour certayne mooſt valyaunt capitayne many ryghteous moderate prynce truely none deceyued nowe fewe dayes paſſed funerall obſequies performed ſeamed good vnto frendes bryng yonge emperour vnto army myght ſpeake vnto ſouldiours vſage newe emperours diſtributyng money largely amongeſt eſtablyſhe theyr myndes wer obligacion vnto therfore commaunded ſouldiours accordynge olde cuſtome ſhoulde repayre togithers fielde whoſe aſſemblie themperour commodus came furthe hauing finyſhed diuine ceremony aſcēded themperiall throne ſame purpoſe myddes campe erected hauing hym father frendes many excellent lerned men ſpake theſe wordes muche lyke enſue ¶i fully perſwadedthe oracion commodus dolour calamite common leſſe ſorowfull ſelfe father lyfe neuer behaued ſelfe ſuperiour vnto loued v equally dyd wyllingly call companion sonne bicauſe eſteamed one name nature reckened participaciō vertue often time caried armes while infante delyuered handes might ſaye gaue wholy vnto cuſtodie fidelyte wherefore doubt ye wyll exhibyte vnto fauour myne elder oughte repute ſonne myne equalles age may luſtly call companyons armes euen ſoo dyd father loue v one prouyded haue v enſtructed exercyſes vertue learnyng nowe hym hath fortune gyuen prince vnto ſtraunger ſome hath bene one whyche vaunteth hym ſelfe conquered empyre onelye borne vnto brought vp verye imperyall palayce ſoone moothers wombe thymperyall purple receyued ſo muche ſooner man prynce ponderynge therefore theſe thynges myndes loue embrace ryghtful emperour gyuen borne vnto father taken vp intoo heauens made companyon wyth goddes vntoo v regymente earthe gouernaunce mortall cauſes doo appertayne ſucceſſe effect ſhall come vnto reſteth youre power ye wyll therefore valyauntly fyniſſhe reſydue warres enlarge romayne empyre vnto ye great ocean ye ſhal onely purchaſe vnto ſelues exceadynge muche glorye alſo duely requyte memorye commune parente beleue verelye nowe heareth v preſently beholdeth doo let v accompte ſelues mooſte happye haue ſuche witneſſe good dedes actes ye haue vnto thys daye valyauntly proſperouſly atcheued attrybuted vntoo hys prudente gouernaunce ſhall hereafter notablye brynge effecte wyth ſaye wyth yonge man emperour ſame ſhall wynne vntoo youre ſelues peculier fame well truth proweſſe whereby ye ſhall brynge myne age eſtymacyon wyth executing boldely oure affayres barbarous people beyng begynnynge thys newe pryncypalitye throughlye repreſſed wyll hereafter ouer boldelye aduaunce theym ſelues deſpyſyng youthe one taught theyr owne peryls wyl reſtrayned kepte vnder wyth contynuall awe feare thus muche ſpoken dyſtrybuted amonges souldyours greate ſumme money myghte thereby confyrme heartes faythefull louynge towardes hym retourned hys palayce lytle ſpace thys thynges ruled hys father frendes tyme abſente wyth theyr prudēt counſayle giuyng hym muche lybertie withall thoughte ſuffycyent preſeruacyon healthe anone certayne themperours houſholde crepte lyttle lyttle forwarde omyttynge nothynge vndoone myghte corrupte good dyſpoſycyon yonge emperoure table paraſytesthe table paraſites meaſured felicytie theyr belies▪ fylthye luſtes enfourmed hym often tymes cytie pleaſures nowe recytynge thoſe thynges whyche delectable hearde ſeene extollynge wyth prayſe abundaunce thynges dyſprayſed beſydes bankes hiſtriahiſtria vnprofytable ſeaſons yt pleaſaūt apple tree fruite enuyroned wyth contynual colde cloudes wylt thou neuer emperour ſayde leaue drynkynge water digged congeled togyther yſe shal mē enioye clere well ſpringes pleaſaunt colde runnynge ryuers holſome ayre italye theſe allurynges wantonneſſe eaſely enflammed yonge man mynde wyth vehemente deſyre thoſe pleſures wherfore furthwyth hauynge called hys frendes togyther dyſſymuled verye deſyrous hys natyue countrey yet fearynge declare cauſe hys ſodeyn alteracyon mynde fayned ſtoode greate doubte leaſte ryche manne nobylytie woulde take poſſeſſyon imperyall palayce thereupon gatherynge vntoo hym greate power mē would oute ye ſtrongeſt fortreſſe chalenge vntoo hym ſelfe princypall domynyon thēpyre ſayd amonges people may eaſely leuied mighty approued cōpany yonge men while thieſe cauſes moued reſt hauing eye caſte vpon earth ſtyll ſorowfull countenaunce pompeianus age mooſt auncient maried cōmodus eldeſt ſyſter aroſe vp ſayed meruayle sonne ſoueraignethe oracion pompeianus vnto commodus holden wyth deſyre countrey ſame deſyre ſeyng oure houſholdes dothe vrge ſturre v alſo repreſſe affection thaffaires haue hande requyre fyrſte parte lyeth v vpon diſpatche pleaſures citye ſhall longer enioye hereafter rome contynually emperour ſoiourneth nowe gyue ouer warre lately begonne beſydes ſhamefull alſo peryllous thereby miniſter occaſion audacitee vnto barbarouſe people wyll thinke departed cauſe recreaciō fledde daunted feare vnto ſelfe howe gloriouſe wyll ye haue vanquiſhed enemy enlarged boundes empyre vnto ocean retourne rome wyth tryumphe therin haue ledde bounde captyues barbarouſe kynges lordes truly ſorte former worldes romaynes noble famouſe cauſe ſhoulde feare affayres city haſarde euery principall ſenatour preſent wyth hole army doth eye defende empire yea chiefeſt treaſoure v alſo memorie beſides father hath eſtablyſſhed ſtedfaſt perfecte beneuolence towardes eſtates pompeianus perſwading hym better thus muche ſpoken ſomewhat preſent repreſſe wyll endeuour younge emperour fearyng olde man ſayinges hauing nothing wherwith myght well replye diſmyſſed counſayle promiſyng would diligently leyſure debate hym ſelfe thoſe thinges yet afterwarde hys ſeruauntes paraſites callynge inſtantely vpon hym made relacion vnto hys counſailours hauyng ſent letter vnto rome appointed thought meete defende bankes hiſter reſtreigne attemptes barbariens cauſed furthwith remouing proclaymed thei lefte behynde diligently executed office appoynted wythin lytle ſpace broughte many ſubiection ſome ioyned great gyftes frendeſhyp vnto whiche verye harde doo barbarouſe people beyng naturally gready money deſpyſers daungers eyther gette liuing wyth inuaſions pylleng neyghbours elles appoynted ſalarie ſell peace thing commodus perceyuyng might money wherof innumerable abundaūce purchaſe hym ſelfe ſecuritee quiet denyed nothing vnto demaunders aſſone fame hys ſetting forwarde ſpredde armye ſodeynly greate ſturre amonges souldyours euery man deſyring returne vnto rome affecting pleaſures citye leue theyr enemyes countrey blowen abroade reporte purſeuauntes poſtes emperour retourning citye incredible ioye wandered amonges common people euery man conceuing hym ſelfe ſinguler hope thēperours preſence truſting aſſuredly would folowe father ſteppes hym ſelfe making ſpeade hys iourney paſſynge wyth certayne feruencie youthe charyot throughe myddes thē city receiued princely reuerence ioyfull aſſemblies people welcomed one moſt acceptable wyſhed vnto approched nygh vnto rome hole senate romayne common eche coueiting preuent crowned wyth lawrell caryeng • ynde flower preſente ſeaſon yere • yd miniſter met farre coulde citye prince notable floure youth nobilitie byrthe truely loued moſt feruent affection beyng borne brought vp amonges nobilite commodus fauſtina commodus mother antonius puis hadrian traian beautie commodus poſſeſſynge thirde degree thempyer regimente rome father ſyde iſſued chiefeſt senatours hys mother fauſtina prince wyfe doughter antoninus pius niece mother vnto hadrian dyd referre pedegrue kynred vnto traian grete graundefather parentage commodus deſcended vnto whome beſydes flowre age giuen alſo excellēcie bewtie congruent ſtature body amiable manly countenaunce pleaſaūt ſhining beames hys eye yelow curled heare whiche came sonne dyd ſo glyſter manye deamed ſame paſſed ſprinkeled ouer wyth golden duſte many alſo eſtemed token diuinyte coniecturing rayes top heade generacion nature gyuen vnto hym ſofte heares beſydes ſprange oute hys cheekes couered flower receyued therfore ſuch emperour wyth ioyfull ſhowtes ſtrawing garlandes flower way paſſed enteryd citie viſyted ſaluted temple fyrſte iupiter goddes gyuen thankes hole senate pretorian souldiours fidelite obſerued towards hym went thimperiall palayce fewe yeres honourably entrete father frendes vſed counſaile affayres thoſe yeres expired cōmytted charge hole empyre vnto cōſtituted capitaine garde italyan named perennes man verie experte ſkylfull warfareperēnes ſame abuſyng age yonge emperour permytted hym corrupted wt ſenſuall luſtes ruffyans takynge vpon hym ſelfe charge horſes horſemē ſo purſuyng without impedimente vnto gate cytye deſtroyed grete parte people remayned within knowing calamytie theyr frendes without ſhutte theyr doores gatte vp roofes toppes houſes threwe downe vppon horſemen bothe ſtones tyles therby fortune ſodenly chaunged horſeman durſte preſente ſtryue people fyghting ſafely aboue againſt thē wherfore many beynge wounded coulde lenger endure turned backes fled many alſo ſlayne throughe contynuall thicke fallyng weapon many ſtriken theyr horſes whiche founderid amongs ſtones throwen downe yea footemē whyche ſtations within cyte finally reygned ſcarſely two full monethes hauing ſhewed perfecte profe goodnes men beynge erected ſinguler hope ſodeynly perniciouſe happe enuyenge vtterly deſtroyed thinges hys notable begynninges enterpryſes whiche lyke greatly profyte men peryſſhed myddes courſe fyrſte adiudged lande vntylled vnoccupied eyther italye place ſoeuer vacant tyme kynges vnto tyllers laborer therof vnto whome alſo gaue tenne yeres fredome tax perpetuall lybertye neyther would ſuffre owne name writtē thempours poſſeſſiones ſayenge themperors common vnto romaynes remytted alſo trybutes whiche tyrauntes inuented get money ryuages ryuers hauēs city commen wayes pathes reſtored aunciente lyberties yt ſeamed alſo would many lyke thynges dryuen oute citye falſe accuſers commaunded puniſſhed whereſoeuer thei wer founde forſeyng mā ſhold troubled thrughe wronge accuſacion therfore ſenate truſted lyue greate tranquillytie bleſſyd eſtate lyfe ſhewed hym ſelfe ſo equall vnto euery man neuer brought hys sonne beynge ſtriplyng yeres emperours palayce kept priuate houſe went ſchole accuſtomed vſage nothinge vnlyke pryuate child inſtructed thinges one meane ſorte neyther dyd bragge ſhew fourthe tyrrannouſe imperyall pompe durynge tyme pertinax lyued modeſtie maners lyfe onely pretoriane sowldyors repynedthinſolencie men armes emperor gard▪ grudginge preſente condicion thinges affected olde ſenſualitye lycenſe behaue ſelues violently ryfle thynges amonge belly bākettes thei conſulted deſtroye pertinax one comborouſe vnto ſette hys place rule romayne affayres ſome wylde wantone woulde gyue verye moche lybertye wherfore ſodeynlie while euery man quiet madde ran great company much haſte noonetide vnto themperours palayce wyth theyr ſpeares extended theyr ſwordes naked thither comming chamberers palayce aſtonied ſodayne matter vnloked fewe againſt manye naked againſte harneſſed men able reſiſte therfore euery man lefte hys ſtacion ranne dyuerſelye hyther thither yet fewe themperours chiefeſt frendes hauinge ſhewed vnto pertynax flockyng togither souldiours perſwaded make ſhyfte ſelfe fleinge call vpon people ayde althoughe counſelled profitably preſente thinkynge ſhamefull thynge vnworthye themperiall maieſtie hys former lyfe committe ſafetie vnto flighte corner determined preuent peryll go furthe amonges truſtyng ſhould perſwade woulde mitigate theyr furyous braynes wente chamber metyng raging souldiours enquyred cauſe ſodayne ſturre willynge ceaſe ſo filthy tumult one abaſſhed wyth peryll retaining graue countenaunce conuenyent themperiall maieſty ſhewing thing appertaining vnto ſuppliaunt ſpake theſe wordes vnto truelye ye ſlea souldyours neyther ye atcheue anye notable enterpryſe griefe allthe wordes pertynax vnto souldiours age renown certainely ſome neceſſarye ende man lyfe appointed charge cuſtodie youre prynce remoue perylles perſon begin murder ſelues defile handes bloude onely ciuyle alſo emperoure take hede ſaye leaſt preſently abhominable time come daungerous vnto ſelues haue cōmitted iniuri offence agaynſt ſorowfull deathe commodus truely ſtraunge die beyng borne manne thynke ſlaine treaſon verely default beyng one ſelues knowe voyde ſuſpycyon thinges committed youre ſelues knewe fyrſt ſo ſuſpicyon roſe happened others reſte although dead yet wyl ſuffre want thynge wil modeſtly mete eſtate wythoute vyolence extorcyon deſyre theſe wordes ſome euen pacified began depart reuerencyng holynes age prince wyth aſſaulte ſlayne commytted wycked dede knowyng people woulde dolefull wente ſtreyghte vnto campe kept ſelues within fortreſſe hauing appointed men armes ye towres kepe people walles end pertynax lyfe maners haue ſayde worthye eternall prayſe rumour murdre ſpred amonges people place fylled tumultes lamentacyons people wandered hither thither lyke madde men vncertayne ſhoulde doo ſoughte aucthours myſchiefe whome could neither fynd auenged eſpeciallye senate meruaylouſe dolefull reputing calamitye yt wāted ſo good father ſoo meeke prynce fearyd alſoo tyranny whyche knewe agreable vnto menne armes daye twoo paſſed commynaltye throughe euerye man perticulyer feare remayned reſte thoſe bare anye aucthorytye departed vnto ſuche manours poſſeſſed furtheſt cytye leaſte choſynge newe gouernoure ſome greuouſe offence ſhould layd charge ye ſouldiours knowynge people quyet manne remaynynge woulde reuenge prynces deathe kepte ſelues wythin theyr fortreſſe hauynge ſet vpon wall one wyth verye loude voice proclaymed empyre ſolde ſayinge woulde delyuer vnto hym woulde gyue moſte money woulde brynge hym ſafelye emperyall palayce proclamacyon hearde neuer moued man senate graue aucthorytye neyther anye manne nobylytye fynallye thoſe ryche beynge fewe number throughe tyrannye commodus neyther durſte anye approche vnto wall purchaſe wt money ſo deteſtable domynyon declared vnto one iulyanus bene conſullthe ambicyon iulyanus ſuppoſed alſo haue great aboundaunce money nyghte whan ſate supper banquetyng reckened man euyll conuerſacion wherupon wyfe hys doughter▪ companye paraſytes perſwaded leauing hys table ſhould make haſt knowe done hys goynge exhorted hym occupie voide empyre affyrmynge might conuynce others gyftes perdye ſo paſſynge ryche wherefore approched nyghe walles cried lowde voyce would giue demaunded ſaying great abundaunce ryches cheſtes full goulde ſiluer ſame time one sulpitianus hadde alſo bene conſullsulpityanus gouernoure cytye father lawe pertynax cheapened empyre menne armes ſuſpected hym affynytye wyth pertynax thynkynge ſome deceyte myght therebye auenge death pertynax wherfore hauynge lette downe ladder toke iulyanus vp vnto walles beynge ſo bolde open gate vntyll accorded paymente money beynge entered fortreſſe fyrſte promyſed woulde reſtore honoures image commodus whyche senate hadde taken downe woulde graunte vnto theym ſame lycence hadde vnder commodus woulde gyue vnto euerye souldyoure money eyther durſte deſyre hoped receyue neyther ſhoulde anye delaye payment ꝙ ſafely kepte houſe promyſes menne armes beynge entyſed trayned wyth great hope pronounced iulyanꝰ theyr prynce gaue hym ſurname commodusiulyanus made emperour bi ye pretoriā souldyours dyſplayinge theyr baners vpon painted pyctures iulianus concluded brynge hym furthe wherefore sacryfyce vſage ended wente furthe enuyroned wyth greater garde emperours accuſtomed hauyng boughte thempyre vyolence agaynſte people wyll fylthye ſhame wt good cauſe feared thinſurrectyon commynaltye souldyours beynge armed compaſſed euerie ſyde like cyrcle nede requyred myghte fyghte toke myddes theym theyr emperoure lyftynge theyr ſhyldes targettes ouer theyr heades therebye ſafer yf ſtones throwen houſes broughte hī thēperours palayce none people durſte reſyſte neyther dyd folowe emperoure accuſtomed ioyful ſhoutes euerye manne curſed hym bytterlye reprouynge hym hadde purchaſed thempyre wyth money fyrſt dyſpoſicyons souldyours corrupted increaſed fylthy inſacyable couetyſe money contempt themperyall maieſtye mā remaynynge woulde reuenge cruell deathe late prynce neyther anye woulde wythſtande fylthye facte ſale vnhoneſte marchaundyſe ſame gaue occaſion vnto menne armes waxe thereafter vnreuerente rebellynge ſo muche auaryce contempte prynce daylye encreaſed euen vnto deathe iulyanus hauynge obtayned thempyre gaue hym ſelfe ryotte neglectynge weake publyke leadynge naughtye voluptuouſe lyfe▪ yea deceyued truſte souldyours beyng vnable performe hys promyſes vnto nat ſo greate ſubſtaunce bragged common treaſure exhauſted immoderate diſpēces commodus theſe cauſes men armes one part deteſted ſide people ignoraunt thereof deſpyſed hym wherefore purſued paſſed reproche vpbraiding hym hys fylthye vnſtable pleaſures ſo opēly theater vnto great multytude men reſortethe thei wold rebuke iulianusnyger called thēpire call nyger ye protector romayne empire preſidēte soueraine principality prayeng hym woulde wyth ſpeade come vnto thē delyuer thoſe manyfolde iniuries ſame niger bene cōſull gouernor siriasyria whyche chiefeſte dignitye tymephenices phenyces regyons vnto ryuer euphrates vnder hys dominion ſomwhate ſtryken ageeuphrates hauynge bene occupyed many weyghty affayres obtayned renowne modeſtye ryghteouſneſſe ſo ſeamed folowe lyfe pertynax whiche chiefly wanne fauor people reſpecte thei often clamour called vpon hym taunting wyth reproches iulianus beynge preſent extollyng wyth prayſes ioyfull ſhowtes nyger abſente whereof niger hearde truſting thinges wold proſper accordyng hys deſyre ſeynge iulianus men armes neglected one violated hys truthe promyſe people contempned man worthy purchaſed hys principalytie beganne hope obtayning empyre fyrſte dyſmyſſed home ſome time ſome diuerſe capytaynes tribune mē armes likewyſe knowledge newes brought vnto rome dyd intēt rumor mighte ſpreade verye broade eaſte ſo ſuppoſed ioyne manye vnto yf ſeamed nat enterpriſe occupyeng empyre diſceite ſuccor deſyred ayde wherfore people aboutes came incontinentlye towardes hym euerye man hym ſelfe beſechynge hym take charge common wealthe furthwyth vpon hym naciō ye sirians naturally vnſtable prone vnto chaunge thinges thei loued nyger exceadingly behaued hymſelfe verye gentely amonges delytynge wyth pleſaunte playes ſūpteouſe ſolempnities sirians alſo owne nature deſyrouſe ſuche ſhewes amonges whome antyochians enhabyting great famouſe cyte throughoute hole yere eyther citie ſelfe elles suburbes celebrate feaſtes playes wherefore ſettyng furthe ſhewes ſolempnytes vnto ſo wanne harte feruently loued hym whiche niger perfectly perceaued hauing certayne daye commaunded men armes preſente people commynge togithers hyghe place purpoſe erected ſaid vnto enſueththe oracion niger peraduenture ſelues know howe gentle dyſpoſiciō hath bene lōge haue cōſulted wēt aboute weyghtye matter neyther woulde haue come furthe ſpeke vnto tyme yf hadde bene ledde eyther myne owne pryuate counſell aſſured hope elles affection ſurmountinge truſte romaynes call interceſſions weary ſtretche helpyng hāde vnto thē ſhould permyt ſo excellente gloriouſe empyre lefte elder nowe ſhamefully deſtroyed preſumtuouſe raſhe thinge medell ſo weightie affayres without occaſion ſo yf mā deny ſuccour vnto thē wante deſyre laſſhe cowardyſe treaſone wherfore purpoſe come furthe vnto myghte knowe youre aduyſe ye iudge beſte done myghte vſe counſellers thys buſyneſſe yf proſperouſlye comme paſſe commodytie thereof ſhall comune vnto mee ſmal rich ſolicite v romain people vnto goddes haue giuen domynion al thinges romaine empyre ſelfe yet wauering man certainely eſtabliſſhed counſayle whych enter aſſured yf conſyder mindes ſuters manne able reſyſte v come thence reporte men armes thē ſelues whome bought thempire faithful vnto yt hath perfourmed promyſe let heare opinion herein while ſpake theſe wordes furth thole armye common people ſaluted emperour auguſtusniger ſaluted emperour clothed wyth purple adorned wyth imperyall veſture beyng ſodaynlye purpoſe founde wyth fyre borne hym conuayed hym fyrſte vnto temple antyoche hys owne houſe whyche nowe pryuate decked wyth imperyall ſignes ornamentes thoſe thinges nyger beyng ioyfull perceyuing mynde romaynes beneuolence al mē towardes thought al purpoſe perfecte plyght ye bruite blowen abrode incontinently al nacyons inhabited ouer againſt europe haſted euery mā ſelfe proffer theyr aſſyſtence ambaſſadours alſo al partes came antioche vnto hymeurope vnto lawful prynce kinges alſo ruler dwelling beyond euprates tygriseuphrates tigrys ſente gratifye hym promiſyng theyr ayde al hys enterpryſes whyche ambaſſadours rewarded wyth greate gyftes thankes dyſmyſſed ſaying vnto neded preſent anye ayde empyre wel ſtrengthened wolde wtout bloudſhed wel gouerne mynd thus exalted wt great hope began neglygent executing yt ſhould deliting ſelfe ye people antioche wt pleaſures ſetting furth ſhewes playes neither thought going vnto rome yt ſhould firſt haue bene done neither certified illyryan army ſhoulde chieflye haue bene vnto hī theſe affaire truſted knew matter would togither romaine nacions orient condiſcende vnto while thus litle regarded affayres fame thereof ſpred amonges pānoniens illyriens al army abiding coaſtes danuby rheyndanuby rheyn pannonyens seuerus defēce romaine empyre againſte barbariens gouernour ye pannoniens wer al ruled one man aucthoritie one named seuerꝰ nacion affrique man vehement diligente furthering affaire accuſtomed leade hard ſharpe life prompt ye inuentiō ſpedy execution thinges ſeing ye romaine empire hang vnſtedfaſt opened pillage deſpiſed one emperour ſluggyſhe cowarde accompt certaine dreames oracle beſides augmented hope diuinacyons thinges come whē came effect obtained report veritie yt whiche ſelfe wrote moſt part bokes life publiſhed theym openlye painted table behoueth ouerpaſſe wtout writing laſt dreamethe dreame seuerus greateſt weight brought moſt hope vnto whē firſt told yt pertinax made emperour seuerus hauinge ended ſacrifice beyng ſworne obedience prince aſſone came home takē dead ſlepe yt dreamed ſawe great gorgyouſe horſe decked wyth emperours ſadell caryinge pertinax hym ſelfe citie ſtrete called sacrum via came vnto thentrye market place vnto people whyles libertie accuſtomed reſort greate aſſemblyes ſemed vnto yt horſe ouerthrew pertynax • nto ye ground offering backe vnto seuerus ſtanding nygh • caried throughe middes market place reuerenced people remayneth ſame place vnto thys day image ſame dreame beyng verye greate made braſſe thys ſorte seuerus beynge extolled mynde thynkynge ſelfe ſollicited vnto thempyre diuine prouydence determyned aſſay myndes souldiours wherfore adioyning fyrſte vnto capytaynes tribunestribun chiefeſt menne armes talke romayne empyre ſayde nygh deſtroied man remaynyng whome mighte valyauntly prudently gouerned inueighyng alſo agaynſt pretorian cohortescohorte pretoryan defiled othe allegyaunce wyth emperours bloude ſayde deathe pertynax oughte reuenged beyng nothynge ignoraunte memorye pertinax fyxed yet myndes illyryan army hys guidinge vnder emperoure marcus obtayned many vyctoryes againſte germaynes beyng lieuetenaūt illiria ſhewed many example vertue proweſſe warre exhibited hys companion muche beneuolence modeſtie meeke moderate gouernaunce wherfore worſhipping memory ye prince greuouſly grudged ſo greate crueltye ſhoulde done vnto seuerus therfore takyng vnto hī occaſion led eaſely whither wolde faining yt affected thempyre ſoughte reuenge bloud pertynax mē ye regyon great tall body prompte redy warre murder ſo dul groſſe capacitie eaſelye perceyue man craftelye ſpeketh worketh therfore whē seuerus faithfully promiſed perſecute murdre pertynax ſo wan al theyr fauours named emperour receiued whole aucthority thē vnderſtode mindes pannoniens immediately allured vnto wt giftes ruler nighe nacions yt ſubiecte vnto romayne empyre seuerus ye redieſt men faine frendſhyppe paſſed periured yf neade requyred alwayes hauynge one thynge mouthe hys ſtomacke therefore gotten credite fauoure letter illyryans ruler prouinces hauyng gathered togyther souldyours euery parte taken vpon ſurname pertynax whiche ſuppoſed woulde moſt acceptable onelye vnto illyrian alſo vnto romaine people hauyng called togither fielde ſpake vnto theym enſueththe oracion seuerus▪ euidētly ſhew ſouldiours loyalty religion towardes goddes bi ye ſworne reuerēce ye bere vnto emperour whē ſo muche deteſt men armes ye citie miniſters rather pompe ſuper fluitie vertue proweſſe haue cō mitted ſo horrible offēce certainly entring ſo great hope ſelues pardie al know obedient haue bene vnto prince deſire atcheue bring effect yt ſhal acceptable vnto neither ſuffre romaine empire runne ruyne whiche gouerned elder wt great aucthoritie reuerenced men fel vnto commodus althoughe throughe youth began manye time decaye yet al fault therof ſhadowed partly wt prynces nobilitie partely wt memorye good father▪ neither vice deſerue rather hate cōpaſſiō imputed ye thinges yt done ſo muche vnto hī vnto ye flattering paraſites counſellers miniſters vile voluptuouſenes vntill thēpire came vnto ye godly olde man memory • e vertue goodnes reſteth yet myndes whō notwithſtā dinge ſo farre entent ſuſtaine yt wc abhominable murder deſtroyed hī hath man know purchaſed domynion sea lande acte hated people neyther men armes true vnto hym becauſe hathe deceyued yf woulde defende hym yet number valyaunte proweſſe compared vnto beſydes haue bene exercyſed warlike affayres accuſtomed fight barbarouſe nacions ſuffer al labour deſpyſe heate colde paſſe ryuerſe froſen ouer yſe drynke water dygged ſpringinge oute yearthe watche hunting wylde beaſtes fynallye furnyſſhed prouiſyons appertayninge vnto valiaūtnes ſo eaſye man withſtāde ſtrengthe man armes approued labour banqueting ryotte yt whiche thei ſo traded thei ſuſteyne youre voyce muche leſſe ſyghte yf affayres siria ſeame terryble vnto man let ſame ponder howe weake wyth howe ſymple hope thei ruled dare come furth cō ſulte goynge vnto cyte taking thoſe habitacions good worthe accompte pleaſures eueri daye goten lucre vnconſtant aucthoritie nacion sirians chiefly addicted vnto ieſtes playes thei enhabite antioche thoughte principallye fauour niger nacyons cytes ſeynge man worthye empyre ſhould modeſtly valyauntely gouerne cōmon wealthe laſte faigned ſelues obey hym yf one knewe emperour created illyrian armye hearde therwithall oure name whyche vnknow vnto ſelfe haue heretofore dominion ouer wyll alledge cowardiſe ſlouthe vnto v neyther abide inuaſions proue valiaūte proweſſe eſpecially ſeyng comparable vnto eyther talnes perſon warlycke exerciſes fyghting hāde hāde wherfore lette v ſpeade poſſeſſe cyte rome verye ſeate thempyre ſhall eaſely bryng paſſe reſidewe affyeng ſelues oracle goddes ſtrength weapon bodyes seuerus ſpokē thieſe wordes vnto receaued hym wyth ioyefull ſhoutes callynge hym auguſtus pertinax promyſed hym beneuolente harte myndesseuerus named auguſtꝰ pertinax thinking good prolonge time cō maunded celeritee armed proclaimed voyage towardes cite gaue vnto euerye manne vytayle ſufficiente neceſſaries iorney remoued ſpeade reſtinge place one ſuffring souldiors ſtaye vntyll throughe theyr greate labour coulde ſcarſely fetche breathe hym ſelfe trauaylinge wyth formeſte lodgynge ſimple tente dyd eate dryncke ſame ſouldyours dyd neuer ſhewinge anye pompe imperyall wantonneſſe whereby euerye daye waxed acceptable ſeynge onely partaker alſo authoure heade theyr trauayle became ſo honourable vnto theim ſeamed mooſte gladde anye thynge woulde commaunde hadde paſſed pannonye come vnto mountaines italy preuenting ſo fame approche open ſight hys commynge harde meruaylouſe dreade inuaded italyen cityes ſawe ſoo greate armye inhabitauntes italye beynge longe ſpace voyde warre dyd nowe tyll theyr lande lyued peace longe cytie free capitaynes warres elected senate italyen nacions euer harneſſe hauynge ſubdued grecian barbaryens gate vnto theim ſelues dominion lande sea neyther anye clymate parte worlde vnto whyche romaynes ſtretched theyr force auguſtus hadde obtayned empyre releaſed italyans laboure toke theym theyr weapon reteyned wyth hym appoyncted wage onely certayne mercenarye souldyours defende romayne empyre compaſſed boundes hys empyre wyth greatneſſe ryuerſe dytches wyth hyghe ſharpe hylles wyth deſerte place wherfore harde seuerus nighe ſo greate armye beyng withoute cauſe vnaccuſtomed thynge aſtonyed durſte neyther reſyſte forbyd hym paſſage thei mette hym crowned wyth lawrell receaued hym theyr cytyes gate beynge opened abydynge longer anye place ſuffyced ſacryfyce ſpeake vnto people kepte hys iorney towardes rome declared vnto iulianus thought hymſelfe vtterly vndonne hadde ſo oftentymes harde power multytude illyryan armye myſtruſted people knewe himſelfe hated neyther great affiaūce garde becauſe deceaued thē wherefore hauinge gathered togither greate ſome money partely hys owne partelye hys fryndes ſo euer foūde eyther temple anye place diſtributed amonges souldiours thereby myghte reconcyle theyr fauour althoughe hadde receaued many ample gyftes rendred thankes interpreting dutie nowe paide one benefite beſtowed furthermore althoughe friendes iulyanus perſwaded lyghte longe garmentes moſt commonlye throwe theyr dartes ſhoote theyr arrowes fleyng awaye many romayne souldyours artyfycers came enhabyte leade theyr lyues thoſe regyons barbarous people learned onelye weare armure alſo forge make ſame seuerus fynyſſhed hys affayres oryente according owne mynd toke ardente deſyre make warre vpon atrenyan kynge conquere realme parthia bothe whyche nyger aſſocyated vnto hym yet deferrynge thoſe warres vntyll tyme begā inuent meanes myght aſſuredly eſtablyſh romayne empyre hym ſelfe hys chyldren nyger diſpatched remained ſauing onely albynusalbynꝰ whyles seuerus abſente buſyed oryent nobylytye wyſſhed albinus emperour becauſe deſcended noble famouſe lygnage ſelfe beyng yonge man great towardnes gentle diſpoſycyon whych entente seuerus knew ſuſpected albinus frendes therefore thei admonyſhed hym beware falſe deſloyall perſon full diſceit treaſon manifeſtly knowen periured vntrue man hauing owne childerne entyſed niger capitaynes betray haue bene partaker without batayle contencion feareth ye goddes whō hath ſo oftē ſworne neither dothe conſyder fauoure laborious trauayles whyche haue wyth ſo greate renowne glorye ſake ſuſtayned aſſuredly ſelfe wanted profites ſucceſſes yea hadde obſerued fidelitee greteſt porcion ben man yf authour myſchiefe ſhall accompted vnryghteous ſo yf reuenge nat iniurye receyued ſhalbe eſteamed manyfolde benefytes honour glory euen ſo let v nowe wyth force ſtrength conuince daunte hys trayterous feable harte tharmy ſmall ilande able ſuſtayne abyde brunte might ſeynge ye haue youre ſelfes hym ſelfe put vpon hys horſe gyrte wyth robe purple ſeyng albynians thoughte ſelues vyctoryous vanquyſſhers ſcattered abrode oute ordre thys freſſhe bande men ſodenlie ſet vpon fynallye lytle albenyans fyeldes albenyans made rode arabye fertyle whence come ſweete odyferous herbes whyche vſe pleaſaunt • vapour perfume hauing deſtroyed mamany city village waſted hole cuntrey entred atrenia thei moued walles towres engyns ſortes omytting nothyng might auaile aſſaulte batterye ſame ſyde atrenyans ſtowtely defended theyr citie ſhootinge throwing downe arowes dartes ſtones wherewith thei crime therfore puniſhed wt vanyſhemēt seuerus countrey man borne aphrique ſome coniecture nyghe kynred vnto hym ſurmyſe rather gratefull vnto hym vycyous lyuinge throughe flowre bewtye youth hym seuerus enhaūſe frō ſimple low degre vnto wōderful abundaunce treaſure giuing vnto hym goodes many condēpned enriched aboue otherthinſolē cye plauti • nu refrainyng admytting gouernaunce empyre whyche rycheſſe lybertye abuſynge omytted kynde cruelty pleaſed hym became outragyouſe anye prynce thertofore raygnynge doughter ſayde dyd seuerus gyue wife vnto sonne antonyne hym ſelfe nothynge ioyful ſame enforced thereunto rather neceſſitye good wyll vttermoſte deteſted mayden father ſo vſed neyther one bed one houſe wyth ſuche wyſe abhorrynge dayly menaced put father vnto deathe aſſoone hym ſelfe ſhould poſſeſſe thempyre whiche ſhe eftſones reported vnto father opened howe greatlye ſhe huſbande diſdaigned ſhe kyndeled mā maruaylouſlye vnto wrathe plautianus perceyuyng one ſyde seuerus decrepite aged many tymes vexed wyth dyſeaſes eſpecyallye gowte ſyde antonius fyerſe ſtoute cruell yonge man became veary fearefull hys threatenynges determyned commyt ſome notable myſchyefe hym ſelfe peryſſhed manye thynges whych enflammed hym wyth ardente ambycyon thempyre weete hys aboundaunce rycheſſe lyke whereof pryuate perſon time theretofore poſſeſſed obedyence souldyoure great honoure enioyed amonges al romaine ornamentes apparaylle wherein wente abrode ware garmente called latus clauus hadde bene twyſe conſull ware alſo ſworde token promocyon dygnitie beyng whereſoeuer went ſo terrible onely vnapproched vnto man alſo yf anye ſodayne chaunce happened meete woulde turne theyr face hym way ſo euer made hys iourneye certayne vſſhers going whiche cōmaunded euerye man auoyde ſtretes man ſo hardye beholde hym turne awaye theyr eye loke vpon earthe seuerus knew ſelfe toke paciently grudged greatlye thereat ſo diminiſſhed muche plautianus aucthoritie endeuored perſwade hym abate ſomewhat leaſt wiſe ſo inſolent arrogancy plautianꝰ therof impacient doubted compaſſe conſpiracy treaſō thempyre ſelfe therfore ymagined thys dryft certayne tribune named saturninꝰsaturninus whiche chiefly reuerenced plautianus albeit ſo likewiſe yet dyd crepe fauoure greater token apparaunce honouryng hym thys man plautianus reckened hys moſt truſty faythfull frende ſuche onely woulde kepe ſecrete cloſe hys counſell execute ſo euer ſhould commaunde therfore ſent euentide hauing remoued al aparte ſayd theſe wordes vnto ¶nowe ꝙ time comethe treſon plautianus wherein thou muſte make perfect thy loue obeyſaunce towardes whiche thou haſte hytherunto ſhewed euidente proofe wherin may ſuffycyently recōpence thy deſertes choyſe gyuen vnto whyther thou wylt eſchew daunger thou ſeeſt become vaſſalle vnto power elli oute hande peryſh wt worthy puniſhment ſtubburne ſtomake feare thou greatnes enterpryſe neither diſmay thy ſelfe name thēperors lawful go alone chaumbers ſlepe yu diddeſt returne night watche thou maieſt eaſely without interruptiō atcheue thou deſyreſte nothinge elles wherin thou ſhouldeſt longer awayt cōmaundement go thy way courte thoughe thou haddeſt ſome priyue weighty meſſage mine becommeth valiaunt man murdre olde manne boy wythin eyther theyr chaumbers thou arte partaker daunger euen ſo eanded thou ſhalt enioy parte greateſt honoures theſe woordes albeit ſomewhat aſtonyed trybunes mynde yet dyd vtterlye confounde expell hys counſell man prompte readye wytte syryan borne moſt parte thenhabytauntes oryent exacte ſharpe iudgementes perceyuynge frantyke folye mere madnes plautianus knowynge alſo able durſt reprehende thynge ſpoken leaſte hym ſelfe ſhoulde furthewyth ſlayne faynyng hadde hearde acceptable vntoo hym fyrſte ſaluted plautyanus emperoure requyred lybell hys hande concernynge commaundemente ſayd murdre vſage tyrauntes hadde wythoute lawfull iudgement commaunded anye manne put vnto deathe gyue charge therof wrytten ſome lytell boke leaſte ſhoulde argumente proofe remayne ſame appoyntmente wyth plautyanus blynded wyth ouer muche couetyſe delyuered vnto trybune boke ſente hym towardes murdre wyllynge hym aſſoone ſlayne bothe prynces facte publyſſhed ſhoulde ſende hym entente myghte ſene wythin themperyal palayce man hearde hys poſſeſſyon thempyre vpon thys couenaunte trybune departed plautyanus wonte paſſed freelye throughe courte ponderynge wyth hym ſelfe perceyuynge howe vneaſye one manne murdre twoo prynces lyinge ſundry chamber fyrſte wente seuerus lodgyng wylled certayne hys pryuye chaumber helpe hym ſpeache emperoure ſayinge broughte newes whych appertayned emyerours ſauegarde made ſpeadye relacyon hereof vnto seuerus furthwyth commaunded trybune let beynge entered emperoure ſayde theſe wordes come hyther emperourethe treaſon diſcloſed ꝙ ſente fyrmelye ſuppoſeth murdre youre perſonne ſelfe bothe wyſſhe wyll aucthoure greate benefyte preſeruacyon youre healthe plautyanus lyinge awayte wyth treaſon thempyre hath appoynted murdre bothe youre sonne onelye wordes wrytynge alſoo teſtymonye whereof thys boke dede promiſed hym accomplyſſhe commaunded leaſt yf reiected woulde haue taken hande nowe preſente bewraye matter vnto leaſte hys preſumptuouſe trecherye ſhoulde oppreſſe vnwares notwythſtandynge trybune ſpake theſe wordes wyth aboundaunce teares yet dyd seuerus fyrſte credyte ſo muche memorye plautyanus loue towardes hym fyxed yet hys breſte yea ſuſpected matter contryued purpoſe thynkynge hys sonne abhorred plautyanus deteſted hys doughter imagyned thys craftye couyne mortall ſlaunder agaynſt hym wherefore hauynge called hys sonne vnto hym beganne rebuke hym hadde deuyſed ſuche myſchyefe agaynſte hys frende well wyller antonyne fyrſte ſware proteſted ygnoraunte thys buſyneſſe afterwardes encouraged trybune whoo perſyſted hys tale ſhewed furthe booke declare hole treaſon trybune perceyuynge intoo howe greate daungere entered ygnoraunte howe muche fauoure plautyanus wyth seuerus knowynge precyſelye yf treaſon laye hydden matter throughly proued ſelfe ſhould receyue extreame cruell deathe ſpake thus vnto soueraigne lordes ꝙ ample argumente perfecte proofe ſeke hereof permytte maye go furthe courte ſome ſecrete truſty perſon certifye plautianus commaūdement fulfilled leuyng wilbe hande occupie palaice voide thē ſhal partes examine trye oute truth thus muche ſpoken choſe faythfull truſtye perſone vnto hym whych ſhould name exhorte plautianus make haſte come furthwith coorte ſeynge bothe prince ſlayne behoued hym deade publyſhed amonges people within palaice therby occupyenge principall tower eſtablyſhenge thempyre vnto hym ſelfe men ſhould maugre harte obey hym one entringe thempyre already poſſeſſed therof plautianus crediting matter puffed meruailouſe preſumption hope putting hym ſhyrte mayle ſure defence hys bodye aboute euenynge ſame daye aſcended hys chariotte made haſte towardes coorte fewe whyche preſent attending vpon hym thoughte hadde bene ſente emperours ſome earneſt weighty buſyneſſe wythoute let manne entered palayce porter beynge ignoraunte matter mente trybune mette hym ſaluted hym emperoure colluſyon purpoſe imagined toke hym hād ledde hym chamber feygned bothe dead emperours corpſes laye nowe hadde seuerus appoynted certayne hys garde laye handes vpon hym ſoone commen plautianus hauinge inſtaunte fāſyes heade entred chamber ſawe two emperours ſtandynge perceyued hym ſelfe apprehended beyng wyth ſo greate matter ſore agaſte began humbly entreate deſyre pardon affyrminge thys dryfte forged vniuſtely malice againſt thē seuerus reproued hym reherſynge manye tolde benefites honor beſtowed hym plautianus replyed agayne repetynge teſtimonies hys accuſtomed truthe good wyll towardes themperour wherwith seuerus began ſome relente credite wordes plautianꝰ vntyll ſhyrte mayle appeared throughe ſlyt vpper garment whiche antonyne perceiuing ſterne fierſe yonge man thertofore deteſting plautianꝰ ſaied wold gladli wete ꝙ anſwere thou wylte make vnto thieſe two pointes cameſt thou euening vnto themperours vnſent meaneth ſherte mayle thou weareſt commeth armure supper banquette hauinge ſo ſaydethe punyſhemēt plautianus commaunded tribune thoſe preſent ſtabbe hym ſwordes dagger manyfeſt traitour open enemye thei makinge delaye mater executed themperours commaundement ſlewe man threwe hys body highe waye ſpurned ſkorned people iuſte ende lyfe plautianus man inſatiable auarice done seuerus conſtituted two capitaynes ouer men armes hym ſelfe moſte commenly ſoiourned suburbes elles nyghe sea coſtes campania ſitting iudgement vpon mater controuerſy lawe beyng diligent ciuile affayres chiefly coueyted haue childerne traded rome decente honeſt maners perceiued theyr myndes bente vnto playes ſhewes vehementlye became theſtate prince wherby wold come paſſe yōge mēs ſtudies cōtencions tending diuerſe purpoſes willes alſo appetite woulde become dyſagreable whē certaine brondes debate ſhold kindled betwene eſpecially antonyne death plautianus wexed terrible vnto al men beſides compaſſed wyth crafte ymaginacions could deuiſe might deſtroy doughter plautyanus hys owne wyfe seuerus ſent lytle sonne whyche ſhe antonine sicilia much richeſſe abundantely ſuffyced meate drincke neceſſaries enſuyng point auguſtꝰ entreated ſame ſort sonnes antonius adiudged traitour seuerus endeuoured coulde reduce hys sonnes loue concorde reconcyle eyther admonyſhing auncient hiſtories example wherin many calamytes riſē thrughe diſcorde bretherne wer reherſed added therunto treaſure ſelfe hadde gathered togither temple filled money richeſſe whiche encreaſed daylye foreyne tribute howe souldiours might abundaunce retayned ample riche gyftes mē armes citye augmented foure time thē thei ſo greate armye ſoiorned nyghe citye forreyn power yf man conſidered ſelfe multitude greatnes body elles abundaunce money could founde comparable vnto thieſe thinges ſayed wolde none effecte while two brother dyſagreed kepte ciuell warre within ſelues reherſall hereof entermedlyng correction praier laboured repreſſe inſolent courage bringe atonement concorde vaine thei throwen brydelles theyr mouthes beyng continually enclyned worſte although yōge men feruencie youth immoderate lycence ſturred much alreadye vnto delytes ſundrye voluptuouſe luſtes yet euer redi elbowes flockes paraſites allured vnto diuerſe cōtrary diſpoſicions extolling diſſolute vice alſo inuēting newe pleaſures wherwith one myght pleaſed offēded paraſites seuerus hym ſelfe apprehended many verye minyſtery theyr flatterye therefore dyd put theim death olde man thus mynde moleſted wyth ſenſuall vnhoneſte lyfe delytes hys sonnes receyued letter hys lyuetenaunte englande wherby enformed barbarouſe people rebelled waſted thole region inuaſions commocionscommocion mutine england wherefore neaded greater puyſſaunce men reſiſte ſuppreſſe wanted sone fourthe citie farre pleaſures therof thei might accuſtome ſelfes warlike ſober dyet wherfore proclaimed expedicion britayne beynge olde ſore troubled goute yet ſo valiaunte ſtomake neuer yonge man hys iorney roade mooſt communely horſe litter neuer reſting longe place ended voyage paſſed ocean sea muche celeritee thoughte entred brytaine muſtered souldiours hauing gathered wōderfull power greate miſchief henge ouer hys heade knowing alſo antonynes wrathe outragiouſe cruelty ſpecially ſhoulde haue ſuche occaſion kepte backe ſame lettre reſte declared contentes vnto themperour yet fearing leſte maternianus woulde eftſones certefye emperour ſame matter determined commyt ſomme acte fourthwyth rather delayeng tyme ſelf ſhould periſh therfore thus cōcluded ther certain cē turiō named martialismartialis one antonines priuey chā ber accuſtomed alwaies next attendaūt perſone whoſe brother antonine put death vpō ſimple accuſaciō wtout leful iudgement vſed tentymes checke martialis himſelf callinge hym cowarde cōfederate macrinus mās ſorow ye death brother macrinꝰ throughly perceiuing knowing alſo ſufficiētly ſtyrred malice reproches called ye ſame one alredy bounde manifolde benefites vnto perſwaded yt ſone could finde oportunite ſhould ſlea antonine martialis beinge wt promiſes allured throughe owne grudge reuenge hys brother death already enflāmed promiſed wēt requiſites nature martialis awaited euery conueniēt howre ſeyng emperour alone farre made haſte towardes though called ſome buſineſſe running vpon vnwares vntruſſing pointes ſtabbed wc dagger companion property wyſe men ſuſtayne moderatly mortall calamityes memorye ſhall cōtinually fixed harte lefte vnto poſteritee wyth eternall commendacion valiaunt actes hym atchyued beſydes hys loue towardes hys partakinge youre paynefull trauayles whyles lyued nowe tyme caſe requyreth hys funeralles due honoure parfourmed prepare ſelues reſyſte daunger imminent ye ſee barbarouſe king hande wonderfull multitude oryentalles hauing ſeameth iuſte occaſion warre fyrſte prouoked breche promiſe mouing war againſt thei quiete tranquyllytie romayne empyre ſtrength lyeth valiaunt proweſſe faithfull allegyaunce doo contende oure owne boudes ryuerſe mighty puiſſaunt kynge muſte nowe fyghte ſaufe garde owne lyues ſeynge comme reuenge murder chyldren kynred ſubiectes v ſlaine thinketh contrarie equitie trueth wherefore lette v nowe fall armes romaynes accuſtomed obſerue iuſte order oure batayles barbarouſe multytude beyng rude oute order may happen thereby ſelues domage order agremente knowledge warrefare defende ſaufegarde euyn ſo doo thei woorke youre enemyes deſtruction would therfore ſhould haulte courage hope victorie ſo fyghte becommeth romains haue cōtinually hitherunto done ſhall ye onelye vanquyſhe barbarous people alſo hauynge obtayned famous renowmed glorye adde vnto romaynes perfecte confidence former conqueſt atchyued fraudulente diſceyte notable valiauntnes ſtrengthe thys muche ſpoken souldiours perceauynge neceſſitye preſente fell vnto armes ſet ſelues order battayle ryſyng sonne ſawe artabanus marchynge forwarde huge armye aſſone barbarous people accordynge theyr vſage worſhypped sonne furthwith ran romaynes wyth mightiea ſore battayle clamorous ſhoute ſhoting horſes manye arrowes dartes romaynes hauyng ſtrongely planted theyr fronte diſtributed maurytanian horſemen eyther ſyde receaued mids theyr battaile dimilaunces lyght horſemen reſiſted valiauntlye barbarous people fyrſte vexed greuouſly multitude arrowes longe ſpeares wher men armes rode camelles horſes foughte ſkirmiſhed thother ſyde romaine ofte moued forwardes eaſelye obtayned better wer oppreſſed barbarous horſmen camelles faining flea planted caltrop engins yron ſharpe thone eand ye groūde whiche beyng hid vnder ſand ſeen man pernicious vnto horſmen thoſe rode vpō cameles fallen ſame caltroppes horſes ſpecially camel ſame beaſt hath tēder hoofes became furthwith lame ouerthrewe theyr rider barbarous people long ſate horſes cammelles fought fierſly eyther alighted ouerthrowen eaſelye taken durſt abide battayle yf ſhould flea purſue theyr enemy thei interrupted longe wyde garmentes retchynge downe theyr heeles battayle continued two dayes mornynge nyghtea longe battayle nyghte ſeuered eyther armye retourned campes conquerours thyrde day met playne preſte daraigne battayle barbarous people attempted thoſe whiche many number compaſſe romains entangle nette romaynes ſeynge ſame ioyned together rounde compaſſe ſet ſelues longe front myghte thereby prohibyte compaſſynge theyr enemy ſo great multitude men beaſtes ſlayne fieldea meruaylous ouerthrowe ouerwhealmed wyth wonderfull number dead carcaſes heaped greate heighte eſpeciallye camelles whyche laye one vpon whereby ſcope ynough souldyours fyghte ſo manye carcaſes heaped togethers coulde ſcarſcelye moue fro wherefore retyred theyr campes nowe macrinus knowynge barbarous kynge golde decked ouches braceletes chaynes kynges golde ware crowne like vnto chaplet adorned golde preciouſe ſtones forme hys habyte meane betwene phenicien median apparayle deſpyſed romaine garmētes doſſolute maners ſhe begā wt hūblepeticiō perſuade ye romayne apparaile leaſt yt yf entred citie senate houſe yt ſtraūge barbarouſe veſture ſhould offēde eye beholder vnaccuſtomed vnto ſuche wātonnes ceputed ſeamely womē mē cōtempning olde woman wordes entending truſt mā retained none perſon ſuche agreable vnto owne ſenſualitye fullye mynding vſe ſame apparayle continually determined wyth beholding ye image continually rode ſo finiſhed fonde iorney leaſt ſhould fall ſlyde vnwares vnwyſe ridinge cauſed ſtretes thicke couered ſāde gard helde hym eyther ſyde might wt ſafty ſit horſe people rā wt torch creſſettes ſtrowinge floures garlādes waie accōpanied beſides pōpe ye image al ye goddes al preciouſe ornamētes wer ye tēples tokēs honor ye beautifulleſt houſehold ſtuffe thempire wt men armes al romayn hoſt brought theſe thinges temple layed ſame finiſhed hys ſacrifice went vp hyghe tower whych wer purpoſe erected threwe manye thynges amonges people weete cuppes syluer golde garmentes ryche worke ſortes lynnen clothe diſtributed amonges alſo kynde tame beaſtes except swyne whyche accordynge phenicien vſage ſelfe abſtained catching wherof many periſhed ſome beynge thruſt deathe preſſe ſome ſlayne wyth souldyours weapon ſame feſtiuall pompe turned dolorous calamitie manye men hym ſelfe beſydes manye tymes ſene cartynge leapynge woulde permitte hys owne flagitious exerciſes hydden goynge often tymes abrode wyth hys eye painted browes made red hys face beynge naturallye beautyful deformed vndecent colour whiche meſa perceaued ſuſpectynge indignation souldiours fearynge yf oughte good came vnto hym ſelfe ſhoulde conſtrayned retourne priuate lyfe ſhe perſuaded fooliſh raſhe yonge man adopte empire hys kynſman neuewe beynge borne doughter mammea ſhe myght better pleaſe hym ſhe ſayde whiche executed office prieſt celebrated ſacrifices goddes ought haue ſome subſtitute ſhould gouerne empire care trouble nowe ther ſtraunger forreyne perſon ſo meete elected thereunto hys owne kynſman ſame alerianus whiche called alexander hys father name chaunged name macedonien kynge ſame kynge great renowne dyd anthonine sonne seuerus chiefelye eruerence whyche anthonine theyr graundemother perſuaded souldyours father blaſyng therby fornication doughters ſhe might therby cauſe souldyours better loue wherfore alexander declared emperoure created conſull wyth antonynealexander made emperoure senate determinyng wyth ſkorne laughter whyche antonyne required ſaye hym ſelfe beynge fourtene yeares olde father alexander whyche vneth entred twelueth yere hys age sonne alexander pronounced emperoure antonyne endeuoured corrupte wyth hys ſenſuall maners ſyngynge daunſynge beynge partaker hys prieſthode ſhoulde weare ſame apparell vſe ſame facions hym mammea moother alexander preſerued hym diſhoneſtye fylthye lyfe bryngyng vp priuely vnder diuers learned men litterature modeſtie good maners accuſtomynge hym vnto wraſtelynge decent exerciſes inſtructynge hym greeke latyn tongue wherat antonine greatly grudged repentinge adoption participation empyre therfore expelled palaice thoſe inſtructours whome ſome excellenteſt put death thother afflicted exile allegyng agaynſt fooliſhe vaine cauſes corrup • ed hys sonne ſuffering hym vſe lybertye daunſynge inſtructinge hym modeſt comelye exerciſes fell ſuche extreme folye diſtributed chiefeſt dignityes common wealthe amonges player commodies enterludes made liuetenaunt generall armye certayne daunſer whiche hys youth bene common player vpon scaffoulds another ſame rabel appoynted gouernour youth another chiefe order knyghthode vnto carter ruffyans diſordered brotheis commytted chiefe charge empyre vnto hys bonde men lybertynes euerye exceaded another abhomination delyuered rule prouynces gaue hym money alſo diſtribute priuelye amonges souldyours whyche chiefelye couete ſame myghte ſure lynked chayne drawe vnto hym antonyne perceaued inuented miſchiefe coulde agaynſte alexander hys moother neuertheleſſe theyr common graundmoother moeſa avoyded ſuche crueltye ſhe woman ſtoute corage alſo longe tyme ſoiourned imperiall palayce wyth suſter seuerus wyfe whereby ſhe throughlye ſkylfull whiche antonyne entended naturallye full talke wythoute diſcretion accuſtomed blaſe abrode ſoeuer mynded woulde haue done ſeynge hys enterpriſe proceade wyſhed determined depriue chylde imperyal honour therefore commaunded ſhoulde longer ſaluted emperoure neyther woulde ſuffer hym go abrode amonges people souldiours deſyred hym wonderfullye diſdaynyng empire ſhould taken anthonine cauſed rumoure blowen abroade alexander deade entente myght thereby perceaue ſorte souldyours woulde take ſame ſeynge chylde appeare abrode hauynge theyr harte perſed wyth thoſe ſorowefull tidynges waxed wonderfull wrothe withelde antonine hys accuſtomed garde hauynge ſhutte gate theyr campe ſayde woulde perforce ſee alexander within theyr temple antonyne beyng thereby ſmitten wyth feare rode vnto campe imperiall chariot beynge adorned wyth precious ſtones wherin alſo ſate alexander whome souldiors bothe entred campe brought temple therof ſaluted aboue meaſure folowynge hym wyth ioyfull
