mē armes senate rome chaū ged moſte peſtiferous tiranny vnto ouerſyght rule noble men ymages goddes whiche anthonine hys lyfe tyme remoued oute theyr seates reſtored agayne theyr owne temple place thoſe whiche anthonine raſhelye • uyll maners aduaunced vnto highe dignity depoſed ſet accuſtomed lyfe occupacion ciuyle foreyne matter iudgemente apoynted thordring wyſe profoūde learned men lawes warlyke affayres cōmitted rule valiaunte capitaines experte men warre thempyre bene thys ſorte greate ſpace gouerned moeſa whiche • ery agedthe deth mo • ſa ended life vnto whome imperial honour appoynted romayne vſage isthe wiſedome māmea ſhe canonized wyth immortalitye death mammea perceauing ſelfe leafte alone vnto sone endeuoured continewe ſame forme gouernement begon ſeynge yonge man enioyed nowe alone thole dominion ſhe feared leſte yonge age ſhoulde walowe extreme liberty thereby fall ſome kinſmans vice wherefore ſhe awayted wel perſon place coorte ſufferīg approched vnto yonge man whoſe lyfe maners ſuſpected leaſt good dyſpoſiciō ſhould corrupted paraſytes flatterer wold prouoke minde appeti • e floriſhing wāton naughty affection perſwaded exercyſe hys body decente recreacions better parte daye often leſte ſhould anye ſpace lefte yll thoughtes whyles myghte better occupyed apoynting thinges neceſſary done naturally beſides alexander gētle meeke diſpoſition bent vnto affabilytie thyng age folowing made apparaunte xiiii yeares gouerned thempyre withoute effuſion bloode muche one man time throughe procurement beyng put death although many greuouſe offence iuſtly deſerued death yet dyd euermore abſteyne execution whiche thing man ſhall eaſely finde emperour eſpecially thoſe whiche ſucceaded marcus man remember whyles raigned without iudgement put deathe accuſtomed reprehende moother blame greatly ſhe ſomewhat coueytouſe money ſeemed ouer gready heaping treaſures taking vpon ſhe gathered money togythers enryche alexander withall yt myght therby abundauntlye beſtowe gyftes vpon souldiours ſhe fylled owne coffer wyth ſame whiche couetyſe blemyſſhed greately themperours honour maugre hys mynde couetouſe woman ſhould catche pyll couine fraude enheritaunce many mē gaue sonne mariage mayden deſcended noble bloode whome notwithſtanding huſbād entyerlye loued ſelfe ſhortlye expelled thimperiall pallaice wyth greate obloquy ſhame coueyting ſelfe onely named auguſta ſhe enuyed cauſe mayden became ſo outragiouſe agaynſte maydens father albeit greate aucthoriſe alexander beyng impacient iniury done vnto doughter hym mammea fledde campe owne ſafegarde ſaying although muche bounde vnto alexander hys manifolde benefites yet muſte force accuſe mammea greate reproche ſhe done vnto ſhe ther wt chaufed cōmaūded ſlaine yt yōge woman doughter beīg thruſt ye imperiall pallaice ſhe exiled aphrique neuertheles done agaīſt ye wil alexāder moother ruled hym aboue reaſōalexāder muche obedient vnto hys moother hī alway obediēt vnto cōmaūdemētes ſo yt one thing may reproued alexā der yt vſed humilitie reuerence towardes mother becam obeyeng accōplyſſhing commaundement againſt hys owne wyll whē ſorte ſpace thirtene yeres raigned tyme alone enioyed empyre tranquillity without diſturbaunce complainte perſon sodeinly loo cam letter siriasiria meſapotamye meſopotamia wherby certified artaxerxes king perſia ouercomen parthianes artabanus theyr king firſte ſurnamed hī ſelf greatartaxerxes waxe twoo crownes onely bereft thoriētal dominion alſo lyfe ſubdued barbarouſe people neighbour made tributary helde ſelfe within riuer tigristygris recouered bāckes therof entred wtin boū de romaine empire inuading pyllīg meſapotamia menacing war vnto siria chalengid scite lande called aſiaaſia europe aegian sea propōtis ſituate ouer againſt europe whiche enuironed wt aegiā sea ſtraites propontis auncient poſſeſſion perſyans bicauſe frō tyme ciruscyrus medes firſt tranſlated kingdome medes perſians vntil raigne darius laſt kyng alexander depriued dominion thorientall coſtes far ioniaionia caria caria gouerned perſian ruler capitaines wherfore affirmed yt duty ſee vnto reſtauraciō ye aunciēt whole empire vnto perſiās whē alexāder heard hereof beīg greatly diſquieted wt thoſe ſodeine tidīges battayle infancie ben traded quiet tranquility noriſhed wt citie pleaſures hauing firſt cōſulted wt frendes counſailours cōcluded ſēde ambaſſadours thoriēt letter ſuppoſed wold repreſſe barbariens hope pacify tumulteouſe inuaſiōs letter ſorte directed behoued artaxerxes holde ſelfe content wt owne boundes limites dominiō ſturre cauſe anye dyſcencion neyther beyng puffed wyth vayne confydence raſhe hope attempte anye greate warre euerye man ought quiet hym ſelfe wyth hys owne ſubſtaunce ſhoulde haue ſuche ſuceſſe hys fyghte agaynſte romaynes obtayned agaynſt hys neyghbours dyd putte hym remembraunce beſydes victory whiche auguſtus traianus lucius seuerus gotten agaynſt wyth theſe letter alexander ſuppoſed reduce barbarous kynge vnto peace concorde throughe feare menace conteyned vtterlye contempnynge ſame determined talke ſet parte trye matter wyth weapon fyghte wyth crueltye foraged ſpoyled whole countrey meſopotamia caryed awaye inhabitauntes bootye aſſaulted ſuche fortreſſes romaynes buylded vpon riuage defende boundes romayne empire man naturally glorious haulty ſtomacke thought ſubdew whole worlde enflamed therevnto wyth proſperous ſuceſſe hys affayres euer without loking obtayned neyther thynges ſmale importaunce whych kyndeled hys mynde coueitynge greater realme hys owne takynge fyrſte vpon hym inuade parthian wyth warre recouer parthian kyngdome many yeres death dariusdarius alexander whome alexander macedonian bereft hys kyngdome macedonian ſelues thoſe ſucceded alexander gouerned ye regiōs orient aſia diſtributed ſundry partes amongs macedonian power greatlye worne ſundrye battayles growen diſcention amonges ſelues arſaces parthianarſaces cyted hyſtories fyrſte perſuader parthian reuolte macedonian conſente parthian barbarous people hys neyghbours wearynge hys head diademe obtayned kyngdome lefte ſame vnto hys poſteritye euen vnto time kynge artabanus whome artaxerxes hauing ſlayne reſtored ſayde kyngdome vnto perſians broughte ſubiection nygh barbarous nacions dyd nowe prouoke romayne power armes relacion made hereof alexander rome determined longer • eare inſolencye barbarous kynge eſpecyallye ſeynge hys liuetenauntes captaynes called hym thyther finallye wyth greate grudgynge ſore agaynſte hys wyll prepared hys expedition orient therfore generall muſters made thoroughout italye prouinces ſuche ſeamed apte eyther ſtature bodye ſtrengthe yeares ſame muſters many muties tumultes amonges romayne subiectes reaſonynge power myghte equall vnto ſo great multitude barbarous people alexander commaunded pretorian souldyours men armes whyche rome repayre fieldes hym ſelfe veynge aſcended tribunal ſeate ſpake theſe wordes vnto theym woulde wyſhe felowes armes make ſuche oration vnto youthe oration alexāder ſhould according accuſtomed wont vnto ſpeaker get loue honour vnto hearer brynge ioye gladnes ſeyng haue many yeres lyued peaceable tranquillitie yf ye ſhal heare new thing lately happened peraduenture ye wylbe feard ſame thynge vnluckelye chaunſed neuertheles becommeth valiaunt moderat men deede wiſhe beſte yet ſuffer take worth ſoeuer happeneth thynge pleaſure ſwete delectable ſo vertue cōmendable glorious firſt geueth occaſion warre ſeameth iniurious euen ſo withſtandeth wronge confident cōſcience conceaueth better hope quarell ryghteous artaxerxes man perſia hauynge ſlayne hys soueraygne lorde artabanus tranſlated hys kyngdome vnto perſians doth nowe enterpryſe contempnynge romayne maieſtie prouoke v battayle inuadynge thys preſent waſtynge oure prouinces endeuoured fyrſte reduce hym gentle letter hys vnſaeiable gredines exhorted hym coueyte owne puffed vp barbarous inſolencye wyl holde hym ſelfe within hys owne boūdes chalengeth v vnto battayle let v therfore tri • le thyng deferre matter bere preſent auncient ſorte souldyours cauſe hym knowe manifolde victory whyche haue obteined vnder gouerment leading seuerus father antonine whiche yong men ſeke coueyte ſay praiſe glorye whereby men maye perceaue knowe onely howe lyue peace quietlye obſerue reuerentlye alſo nede requireth fyght valiauntly touchynge barbarous people theyr vſage purſue vehementlye ſuche fyrſt flee recule euen ſo doo themſelues tourne theyr backes vnto thoſe whyche manfully perſiſt fyght loke anye victorye fyghtynge playne batayle vſynge inuaſyons rodes accompte ſelues conquerours gette ſtelth robberye contrarye parte haue thynges decked meete warres wherewyth haue learned ouerthrowe vanquyſhe alexander hadde ſpoken theiſe wordes men armes receaued hym ioyfullye ſhoutyng ſhewynge theym ſelues readye goe wyth good wylles warre diſtributed greate summe money amonges theym commaūnded prepare ſelues iourney anone made lyke oration senate houſe appoynted daye hys departure whiche beyng commethe departure alexā der frō rome acccordinge auncient vſage fyniſhed hys ſacrſfice departed senate romaine people conueyyng hym rome vpon loked backe wyth wepynge eye neyther anye common people whyche watered hys plantes beholdynge hys departure multitude deſyrous hym becauſe broughte vp amonges gouerned thempire verye manye yeares wyth muche modeſtye departed vſed dilygent ſpede iourney viſited illirian people men war encreaſed hys power euery wēt vnto antioche citie prepared ſuche neceſſaries expedient warres cauſed hys souldiours exerciſe ſelues feates armes ſelfe prouyded wyth muche dilygence weapon harneſſe ſame ſemed good vnto hym proue another ambaſſade whether perſian kynge woulde condiſcende vnto peace vnitie beynge hym ſelfe preſente lytle doubted eyther perſuade artaxerxes woulde leaſt wyſe put hym feare wyth menace barbarous kynge diſmiſſed romayne oratours home agayne wythout thynge concluded theyr companye ſent fourtye goodlyeſt men ſtaturethe ambaſſade artaxerxes hys armye gorgiouſlye apparelled ryche robe adourned wyth gold rode vpon great courſers caryed great bowes theyr handes thynkynge abaſhe romaynes wyth ſyghte theyr talnes ſumptuous rayment effect theyr ambaſſade great kyng artaxerxes commaunded romaynes wt theyr emperour depart syria al part aſia ſituate ouer againſt europeionia caria aegeanſea pontus ſuffer perſians raygne haue dominion farre ionia caria ſuche lande aegean sea pontus doo enuiron theſe fourtye ambaſſadours declared meſſage alexander commaunded apprehended toke al ſumpteous apparail ſēt phrigia alotted vnto thē certayne vilages fieldes tyll enhabit beynge ſatyſfied wyth punyſhmente exyle natiue countrey rekened cruel nothing agreable māhood put thē death thexecutynge theyr maiſters commaundemente beyng taken battayle thieſe thynges thus ended while alexander buſyed preparacion bridge paſſe ouer ryuers leade romayne armye confynes barbariens reuolted fledde frō hym many egiptian souldiours siria alſo dyuerſe commocions beganne kyndle agaynſte hys gouernemente ſame furthewyth appeaſed rebelles taken put deathe alexander ſente certayne armyes souldiours nigh regiones thereby inuaſions ye barbarouſe people myghte eaſylye reſtrayned whiche thynges beynge thus ſette ordre greate armye leuyed thoughte would equall power vnto hys enemyes hoſtethe armye alexander deuided three partes armenia median tigris euphrates deuyded hys friendes counſayle three ſundrye armyes whiche one commaunded marche towardes northe throughe armenia whyche reputed frendely vnto romaynes inuade border median army ſent towardes north alſo commaūding paſſe thoſe fyeldes barbariens tigris euphrates receyued greate maryſhes pooles thereby vncertayne ende thyrde parte hym ſelfe promyſed lede betwene bothe armyes agaynſte barbaryens thynkynge meanes oppreſſe ſodeynly wyth dyuerſe inuaſyons vnready loked ſuche chaunce ſuppoſed alſo perſian power ſhoulde throughe thoſe dyuerſe encoūtres wyth romaynes euerye ſyde dyſperſed abroade faynte entre battayle wythoute order barbariens vſe anye mercenarye souldyours romaynes accuſtomed neyther haue anye armye pytthed campe myghte exercyſe theym ſelues feates warres hole multytude men yea often tymes woman alſo doe aſſemble togethers kynges commaundemente whyche multitude warre fynyſhed dyſmyſſed home agayne theyr pryuate habytacions caryenge wyth theym ſuche bootye battayle euerye one theim hys parte canne gette thefte thei occupye bowes horſes onely battayle romaynes wonte euen theyr chyldehoode brought vp togythers traded wyth hunting bearynge alwayes theyr quyuers arowes wyth thei neuer lyghte theyr horſes whether thei fyghte battayle hunte wylde beaſtes thys polycye alexander albeit fyrſte ſeamed wythoute controuerſye beſte yet fourthewyth fortune made deſtytude good ſucceſſe armye commaunded marche armenia hauynge wyth greate payne diffycultye althoughe ſommer ſeaſon cauſed theyr iorney meatelye tollerable paſſed ſharpe mountaynes craggye rockes entred medium burnte vilages draue away great bootyes one thing relacion hereof made perſyan kynge came reſcue countrey wyth greate power coulde leuye coulde dryue away romaynes thence ſame craggye countrey miniſtred ſure footing eaſye paſſage vnto romayne footemen barborouſe horſemen throughe ſtepenes ſharpe rockye mountaynes hadde vneaſy trauayle laboriouſe iorneye declared vnto perſian kynge armye romayns entred ſuche border parthian extended towardes orient wherefore fearynge leaſte romaynes hadde conquered parthian woulde inuade perſia alſo lefte greate garyſon behynde hym ſeamed ſufficiente defence medium hym ſelfe wyth thole armye made ſpeedye haſte thorientall coaſtes romayne armye marched forwarde verye ſlowelye manne reſyſted theim thynkynge alexander wyth thyrde parte theim wherein chyefeſt menne warre alreadye entred myddes barbaryens therefore reſted ſelues iudgynge beſte make greate haſte ſeynge nowe ſafetye knewe place wherein ſhoulde altogether meete wyth theyr bootye pryſoners alexander deceaued theimalexāder deceyued armye neyther came hym ſelfe broughte anye armye forward doubtfull whither ſo ſlacked feare puttynge hys lyfe haſarde defence thempyre whether hys moother deteyned hym home throughe womanly fearefulneſſe ouer muche loue sonne deade ſhe blemyſſhed blunted hys noble valyaunte courage perſwadynge hym rather ſende furth warres ſtande hym ſelfe battayle whyche thynge dyde vtterlye betraye romayne armye entered barbarous regyons perſyan kynge dyd meete ſette vppon theim vnreadye lookynge ſuche chaunce wyth hys hole power encloſynge theim nette dyd vtterlye dyſcomfyte ouerthrowe euerye perſonne theim beinge fewe number able reſyſte ſo great hoſte theyr enemyes neuertheleſſe fyrſte thei defended ſtoutly targettes weapon naked place theyr bodyes violent ſhot arrowes accomptynge ſelues happely dealte wyth yf wythoute anye playne battayle myghte ſafely eſcape domage thei lytle ſpace encloſed theim ſelues wyth theyr targettes aſſaulted lyke vnto walled cityethe romaynes vanquiſſhed ſlayne euery parte hauynge vnto ende valyauntly reſyſted murdered downe ryghte meruelous calamitie vnto romayns lyke whereof age remembred thei nowe loſte greate armye worthy eyther loyalte ſtrengthe compared vnto anye auncient hoſte paſſed wyſhed ſucceſſe thieſe affayres enhaunſed mynde perſyan kynge wyth hope greater enterpryſes whereof alexander heard beynge tyme verye ſore ſycke eyther throughe peſyuenes myndethe army waxed wroth wyth alexander el thintemperatnes ayre toke verye greuouſlye thole armye waxed wonderfull wrothe agaynſte themperoure thei ſayde theyr companyons betrayde hym throughe hys lyenge performenge promyſe alexander beynge impaciente hys dyſeaſe heate ayre thole armye alſo vexed wyth ſyckenes eſpeciallye illyrian accuſtomed vnto moyſte coulde ayre feading largelye fell throughe ſyckenes danger deathe determyned retourne vnto antyoche whyther cauſed hys souldiours alſo come verye fewe numbre remaynynge mooſte parte theim peryſhed throughe ſharpenes wynter mountaynes handes whiche attendaunt vpon hys perſonne hym ſelfe ledde backe vnto antioche hauynge loſte manye alſo wherfore thys matter broughte muche ſorowe vnto armye greate diſhonour vnto alexander fortune hauynge deceaued hym place tourned hys entent none effecte meruaylous numbre thoſe iii army ſo perdye deuided deſtroyed diuers calamity ſyckenes battayle colde alexander come vnto antioche recouered health refreſhed wyth temperat ayre aboundaunce water burnynge heate meſopotamia refreſhed alſo hys souldyours cō fortynge theyr ſorowe wyth geuynge theym money whiche rekened pryncipall meane winne theyr heartes renewed hys armye repayred ſame wyth freſhe souldyours throughout though woulde one leade agaynſte perſyans yf proceaded troubleſome deſiſted iniuries declared vnto hym perſyan kynge hadde dyſmyſſed hys souldyours home theyr habytacions althoughe barbaryens ſeamed superyours battayle yet throughe often ſundrye batayles foughte medium parthia great parte ſlayne reſt whyche remayned eyther empayred wyth dyſeaſes elles skyrmiſhes ſore wounded neyther romaynes flowlye ouercome ſelues many time noyſome vnto theyr enemyes beynge none meane vanquiſhed fewer numbre entrapped almoſte lyke numbre bothe ſydes ſlayne reſt barbariens ſtrength proweſſe onelye multitude ſeamed better whereof ſufficient profe barbariens iii iiii yeres fell againe vnto armes whyche alexander vnderſtode made hys abode ſtyll antioche thence forwarde merye liberal forgettyng care warres gaue ſelfe voluptuous pleaſures ſame cytye while thought barbariēs would frō thence furth remayne quiet leaſte wyſe woulde longe tyme coulde aſſemble againe power vneaſy bring together ſeperated rude order rather multitude rural people armye hauing onely much vitaylewhat ye perſiās armie euerye man bryngeth preſēt neceſſitie frō houſe vnwilling alſo depart frō theyr wiues child habitaciōs loo furthwith came meſſengers letter vnto ruler illiria troubled hym wōderfully caſt great thought perplexitie mynde ſignified germaynes paſſed ouer rheynethe germaines rebell danowe entered boundes romaine empire aſſayled army defended banckes made theyr rodes countrey city vyllages great power men thereby illiriās nacion borderer neighbour vnto italye ſtode great haſſarde daunger wherfore requiſit themperour ſhould ther hys owne perſon brynge power wyth hym theſe newes ſtrake marueylous feare alexander doleful ſorowe illirian souldyours perceaued ſelues afflicted wyth two miſerable calamity one inſtaunte hauing fyrſt euil ſucceſſe warres againſt perſians hearyng frendes ſlaine home germaynes wherfore greatly grudged againſt alexander yf hys cowardyſe theyr former affayres bene betrayed thorient protracted remoue northerne cauſes earneſtly called hym ſtode alexander hys frendes greate doubte italie affayres perſians germaines beyng vnlyke daunger thoſe inhabite orient ſequeſtred wyth great diſtaunce lande sea thereby ſcarſelye heare name italy illirian nacions dwellynge ſmale ſtreyte poſſeſſing verye lytle groundethe scituatiatiō illiria ſubiecte romaynes doo onelye make ſeperacion betwene italye germanye wherfore cauſed hys departure proclaymed agaynſt hys wyl ſauynge neceſſitye conſtrayned hym therevnto hauyng left behynde hym many men ſeamed ſufficient tuition romayne lymittes fortifyed cytyes caſtels ſtrōg garriſons hym ſelfe departed ſpedelye agaynſte germains wt reſidue hys hole armie hauinge wyth ſpede eanded iourneye pitched campe vpon banckes rheine made prouiſion al neceſſaryes belongyng warre fyrſt made bridge shippes galleyes ouer rheyne danowe romaynes myghte paſſe ſyde ſame thoſe twoo counted greateſt ryuers northerheine danubie whych one paſſeth germaynes pannonians sommer ſeaſon nauigable wyth large depe channell wynter ſo harde ouerfroſenpannonye ridden vpon field iſe channell ſo ſtronge harde onelye beareth hoofes horſes feete men alſo whyche come fetche water bryng wyth thē ſo many cuppes pailes doo hatchettes mattockes haue therwith brokē iſe cary ſame away without veſſell ſtone suche nature thoſe ryuers alexander dyd ſet battayle agaynſte germaynes manye mauritanian greate power archer whyche broughte oute orient ſome theym beynge people called oſroheniansoſrohemians reſte parthyan fugytyues whome hadde allured money vnto thoſe souldiours dyd moſt diſpleaſure domage vnto germaines bycauſe mauritanian ſhoote theyr arrowes farre quycke nymble ſwifte ſkyppe fro beyng archer eaſelye ſtrike bare heades germaynes theyr greate bodyes appoynted marke butte often tymes alſo foughte playne batayle hande hande whence germaynes often tymes departed nothynge inferiours vnto romaynes alexander beynge wyth theiſe trouble occupyed concluded ſende oratours vnto entreate peace promyſynge money geue thē whatſoeuer neaded wyth great aboundaunce treaſure germaynes chiefelye greadye money often tymes ſame doo ſell theyr peace romaynes wherfore alexander endeuored bye peace rather haſarde matter batayle romayne souldyours grudged greatlye waſted theyr tyme vayne wythoute occaſion atchieuyng thynge whereby myghte ſhewe theyr valyaunte corage whyles alexander gaue hym ſelfe cartynge ſayde voluptuouſnes expedient reuenge ſelues vpon germaynes punyſhe theyr preſumptuouſe audacitye armye one maximinus certayne village thrace obſcureſt wyth allmaximinus ſhepherd man halfe barbarous whyche youthe bene shepherde hys yeares beynge encreaſed heyghte hys bodye hys myghtye ſtrengthe waged horſeman finallye fortune leadynge hym hande goynge hym aſcended degree offyces warre aſpired vnto gouernement armie prouinces thys maximinus therefore hys experte knowledge warrefare dyd alexander ordeyne gouernour youthe exerciſe feates warre make apte vnto fyghte omyttynge dilygencemaximinꝰ lorde souldyours ſo behaued ſelfe office gayned fauoure thole army onely inſtructynge ſuche thinges dayly done excecutyng hym ſelfe fyrſt deades wyth preſente vſe required onely scolers alſo cō panions hys proweſſe ioyned vnto hym wyth ſundrye gyftes kynde honour wherefore yonge men greateſt parte pannonians beynge ioyefull valeauntnes maximinus opēly ſpeake againſt alexander ſaiynge yet vnder hys moothers aucthorytye dyd thynge commaundemente ſettynge forwarde warres verye ſlowelye much cowardiſe thei repeted oftē within ſelues greate myſhappe receiued thoriente throughe delayes reprehended done nothyng valeauntly agaynſt germaynes wherfore prone nature chaūge thinges greued ſo longe contynuaunce regiment whereof receyued lytle lucre ambition longe aboliſhed aſſuredlye truſtynge ſome prynce ſhoulde attayne vnto soueraignitie without lokyng woulde beſtowe ſome giftes honoure vpon thei concluded murder alexander afterwardes create maximinus emperoure beyng companion armes exercyſes ſkyl warfarre moſte apte warre preſently hande wherfore hauing ſundry bandes aſſembled fielde maximinus came amōges inſtructe yōge souldiours clothed hym purple ſaluted hym emperour doubtfull wether ignoraunte dryfte el made pryuie vnto matter fyrſt refuſed reiected purple ſaw mē armes drawe furth ſwordes threating kyll wiſhing rather daūger come peryll preſente toke honoure vpon hym proteſtynge althoughe ſame fortune erſte dreames viſions ſhewed vnto yet nowe vnwillyngly enforced thē receiue onely becauſe would obey myndes wylled theim appoynte thynges would ſelues taking weapon preuenting rumor matter goo ſlea alexander ignoraunt done thereby souldiours garde hys perſon beyng ſodeyne chaunce diſmaied ſhould either willingly aſſent vnto el beyng vnready loking ſuche happe ſhoulde maugre theyr heades brought ſubiectiō enflamed good willes towardes dublynge wage promiſyng geue greate rewardes pardon punyſhmentes ledde vnto alexander pauyliō incontinētly farre diſtant frō thence thieſe thinges declared vnto alexander greatly diſmaied wt noueltye thereof ran tent mad man weaping trēbling callyng maximiuus deſloyall periured perſon reckening benefytes ſelfe beſtowed vpon accuſing yonge souldiours neglecting othe would enterprice ſo perniciouſly facinorouſe facte fynally offered giue thei woulde deſyre amende ſuche thinges amiſſe souldiours apartayned ye garde hys perſon making ioyfull acclamaciōs vnto promiſed defende might power night one paſſed daye began dawe certaine souldiours brought worde vnto maximinus hande myght ſee duſte rayſed heare noyſe greate multitude farre wherefore alexander came agayne fielde called togythers souldiours beſeaching ayde defende whome ſelues brought vp whoſe raigne ſpace xiiii yeres liued without diſcention hauynge moued compaſſion willed theim arme ſelfes ſtande ordre batayle reſyſt enemy souldiours althoughe thei promiſed ayde vnto prince dyd wtſtanding ſhrincke away lytle litle theim required captaine garde alexā ders frendes put deathe alledginge occaſion commociō accuſed hys moother ſhe coueteous woman heaping hording money throughe pynchynge ſparynge greedy keaping souldiours broughte alexander dyſdayne wyth thus ſtode talkyng moued yet ſoone tharmy maximinus ſyghte encoraged forſake fylthy woman weake yonge man whiche lyued yet vnder moothers commaundemente ioyne ſelues vnto ſtronge valeaunte man theyr companion armes exercyſed contynually wyth feates warre furthwith thei togethers reuoulted frō alexander one aſſente ſaluted maximinus emperour alexander fledde backe agayne pauilion trembling halfe beſydes hym ſelfe embraſyng moother reported blamīg ſuffered calamity ſake aboade loking murderer maximinus created emperour thole armye gaue charge tribunetribun capitaines murderinge alexander wyth hys mootheralexander hys moother wt theyr frendes ſlayne whych ſhould make anye reſyſtaunce thei furthwith entering vyolence pauilion ſlew alexander moother hys frendes euerye noble man excepte fewe whyche lytle made ſhyfte theim ſelues fleeing away hyd corner ſhortly apprehended maximinius dyd put death ende lyfe alexander hys moother hadde ſpace xiiii yeares reigned withoute complainte citezins yea bloodſhead eyther deteſting crueltye murder permitted man ſuffer withoute iudgemente condempned ſo muche addicted gentle beneuolence yf coueyteous greadye moother fylthy couetiſe defamed sōne coulde nothynge haue bene wantynge wyſhed hys gouernement thempyre ¶ argumente ſeuenth booke herodyan begynninge ſeuenth booke maketh mencion maximinus crueltye paſſed ouer made warre vpon germaines returne rome oppreſſed people wyth greuous exaccions commytted much ſacrilege whiche cauſed muche hurley burley amonges people nacion aphrique rebelled made gordianus emperoure vanquyſſhed capellianus gouernour mauritania gordianus deathe howe senate elected maximus albinus yonge gordianus audacytie gallianus foloweth myſchiefe enſued therevpon ¶the ſeuenth booke hyſtorye herodyan haue former booke lēgth declared ſort alexander behaued ſelfe duryng xiiii yeres raygne whoſe death maximinus hauyng obtayned type regimente impyre altered eſtate thynges abuſed verye cruellye hys obtayned power ſo frome gentle gouernemente endeuored chaunge vnto cruell tyrannye perceyuynge ſelfe odious vnto men bycauſe fyrſte aſpyred vnto fortune frō baſe eſtate beſydes beynge aſwell barbarous maners nature greadye bloudſhed endeuoured chiefelye eſtablyſhe empyre vnto hym crueltye fearyng leaſt ſhould contempte senate romaine whyles hys preſent fortune obſcurenes hys byrthe ſpecially noted hym openlye knowen vnto men ſhepherde mountaynes thrace receaued amonges ſymple baſe souldyours region greatnes ſtrengthe hys bodye nowe exalted vnto romayne empyre fortune myghte ſaye leadynge hym hande wherefore fyrſte rooted oute senate houſe frendes councelours alexander whyche ſome dimiſſed romethe tyranny maximinus ſome depriued theyr offyces accuſynge former adminiſtration therein dyd entente myghte alone armye hauynge man nobilitye nyghe hym wythoute reuerence anye ſuch ſtrong fortreſſe exerciſe hys tyranny dyd expell oute imperial palaice al seruauntes alexāder ſo many yeares retayned ſeruice put ſome death fearing treaſon becauſe perceaued dolefully lament death alexander tyranny augmented thorough opening certayne conſpiracie agaynſt hym wherin many captaynes whole senate confedered certayne man nobilitie conſul named magnusmagnus ſame accuſed vnto maximinus entended treaſon againſt perſuaded souldiours tranſlate empyre vnto thys counſayle ſuppoſed ſuche maximinus made brydge ouer ryuer paſſe agaynſt germayns hauyng gredy appetite gottē thempyre vnto warlike affayres erected vnto thempyre huge quantitie bodie ſtrength ſkill warfare endeuoured open deades confirme ye ſame opinion ſouldiours proue therby feare cowardiſe ſlouth alexander warlyke exerciſes iuſtly condempned wherfore omitted nothynge appertayned exerciſe men warre beynge hym ſelfe daylye armes dyd therewith greatlye prouoke courage souldyours aforeſayde brydge fynyſhed determined paſſe ouer germayne reported magnus entiſed great nū ber souldiours excelled prowes eſpecially thoſe vnto whō cuſtody bridge committed aſſone maximinus paſſed vnto ſyde riuer ſhould throw downe bridge exclude retourne thereby betray vnto germains ye depth breadeth ryuer ſuche ſeamed vnpoſſible hym gette ouer agayne eſpeciallye becauſe kynde veſſell ſhore suche rumor thys enterpryſe vncertayne whether ſame truelye reported el forged purpoſe hard giue reſolute iudgemente therein bycauſe wythoute anye tryall aunſwere ſentence manye onelye ſuſpected putte vnto deathe ſame time began great commotion oſrohenian souldyours alſo beynge verye ſorowfull deathe alexander happe meatynge wyth one hys frendesquarcinus named quarcinus lytle hadde dimiſſed maximinus campe tooke hym agaynſte hys wyll loked ſuche matter elected hym theyr captayne clothed hym wyth purple caryed fyre hym ſo adorned wyth perniciouſe honour exalted hym vnto dygnitie emperoure whyche man ſhortelye ſleapynge hys pauilion one hys owne companion ſuppoſed hys frende trayterouſlye murdered ſame named macedoniusmacedonius whyche ruler oſrohenians preſent fyrſte authour vnto reuoltinge maximinus althoughe cauſe grudge betwene quarcinus yet dyd thus murder hym whome hym ſelfe fyrſte compelled become emperour thynkynge ſhewe maximinus ſome great pleaſure caried vnto hym head quarcinus maximinus albeit glad facte hys enemye rydde oute waye yet dyd putte vnto extreame deathe thys macedonius whych loked ſome greate rewarde hoped receaue great thankes hys trauayle becauſe authour rebellion murderer one whyche hym ſelfe induced maugre hys head vnto miſchiefe falſe vnto man whyche moſte affyaunce hym theſe cauſes therfore dyd exaſperate mynde maximinus kyndled hys furye beynge already hys owne nature ouer prone vnto crueltye beſydes horrible viſage ſo huge myghty ſtature none moſt valiaunt grekes moſte warlyke barbariens myghte compared vnto hym theſe thynges thus ſet order gathered together whole armye paſſed wythoute feare ouer brydge made battayle vpon germaynes folowed hym wonderfull nomber men almoſte power barbariens wyth theym verye manye mauritanian slyngers archer folowed hym beſydes oſrohenians armenian one nacion beinge ſubiecte vnto romaynes aſſociated frendſhyppe wyth accompanyed wyth manye parthian beynge hyred fugityues theyr natyue countrey el taken warres ſerued romaynes thys multytude people fyrſte leuyed alexander augmēted exerciſed maximinus slyngers archer ſeamed verye profytable warre agaynſte germayns bycauſe coulde eaſelye ſtryke theyr enemyes vnwares recule theym ſelues furthewyth ſure defence maximinus beynge entred wythin hys enemyes lande fyndynge man reſiſt hym germaines fledde pylled foraged countreye corne beynge rype permitted souldyours burne deſtroye vyllages deade townes houſes verye muche ſubiecte daunger fyre amonges germaynes buyldynge wyth stone tyle verye rare ſcarce wyth great peices tymber ſet earthe ioyned together thycke woodesthe germaynes houſes make tabernacle maximinus goynge forwardes waſtynge countrey ſackyng corne diſtributynge cattell whyche taken amonges souldyours founde yet anye hys enemyes abondoned fielde playne countrey place deſtitute tree hydde ſelues couertly woodes mariſhes thei myght fyght ſodeyne aſſaultes inuade enemyes becauſe thickeneſſe nygh growing togither tree ſeemed become great impediment vnto arrowes dartes theyr enemy thei thought depth maryſhes pooles would daūgerouſe vnto romaynes thei ignoraunte paſſages countrey vnto themſelues eaſye profytable becauſe wading daily vp knee perfectly knewe whiche paſſable foordes whiche vnpoſſible get ouer truly germaines verye cunnynge ſwymming men onely ſwymme bathe ſelues ryuers theiſe place therfore battayle begon fyrſte romayne emperour enterpryſed confllycte valiauntly thei come vnto greate broade maryſhe within germaines retyred ſelues romaine beinge afearde purſue enemyes maximinius fyrſte entered vpon great courſer maryſhe wher horſe foūdered ye belye ſlewe great māhode many barbarous people whyche reſyſted wherefore reſydue tharmye beynge pricked wyth ſhame yf ſhoulde forſake emperour nowe fyghtynge aduentured theim ſelues alſo maryſhe ſlayne many eyther parte ſo barbarien lefte lyue romayne emperour fyghtynge moſte valyauntlye whereby maryſhe beynge fylled wyth deade carcaſes lake beynge myngled wyth bloode cauſed ſeame thys foote battayle foughte wyth ſhyppes vppon water victory wyth hys ſtoute mightye factes onely ſygnifyed vnto senate people rome letter alſo beynge printed great table cauſed publyſhed coorte romaynes myghte onely heare hys valyaunte deades alſo haue theim perfectly expreſſed theyr eye ſame table reſte hys honour senate afterwardes pullyd downe abolyſhed manye ſkyrmyſhes batayles foughten wherein hym ſelfe throughe hys fyrſte gyuynge onſette manfull fyghtynge gate euer price renowne retourned againſt wynter ſeaſon pannony wyth manye pryſoners greate bootye catayle wynterynge wythin cytye syrmiumsirmiū whyche greateſt cytye countrey prepared neceſſaries hys vyage agaynſt ſprynge time threatnyng wholy ſubdue barbarouſe nacions germaynes euē ocean whiche thing ſeamed woulde aſſuredlye brynge paſſe ſuch one affaire warrefare ſhuld haue obtayned wonderfull glory hys factesthe exaccions maximinus yf hadde bene outragiouſe hys owne ſubiectes hys enemyes purpoſe barbariens ſlaine yf much murder commytted wythin cytie ſelf rome nacions ſubiecte thereunto auayleth haue plentye captiues prayes beaſtes yf hys conqueſtes fortune romaynes theim ſelues dyſpoyled haue onely free lybertye alſo entyſynge giuē vnto perniciouſe promoter accuſe cyrcumuente wyth fraude whome thei would yea renewe yf neade faultes done men aunceſtours ſome vnknowen vnharde vntyll preſent inſtaunt neyther man detected anye offence ſame furthwyth condempned goodes confyſcate whereby man myghte daylye ſee dyuerſe whiche wonderfull ryche welthye nowe begge theyr breade greate couetyſe hys tyrannye whyles dyſtrybuted money continually amonges menne warre eares beſydes open vnto complayntes ſo regard mās age dignitie manye capytaines armyes gouernours prouinces wyth dyuerſe hadde bene counſulles theyr merites tryumphed one anye fonde trifle lyghte cauſe accuſed cauſed furthwyth apprehended puttynge theim chariottes alone wythout seruaunte attendynge vppon theim compelled theim come oute eaſte weſte yf chaunce ſo happened oute southe alſo vnto pannony hym ſelfe ſoiourned ſpoylynge theim theyr ſubſtaunce entreatynge theim wyth moſte ſhamefull ſclaunders afflycted theym wyth death banyſhemente longe one two ſuffered thieſe domages ſayde calamity paſſed theyr lynage common people lytle regarded aduerſe chaunces ryche welthy menne onely common neglected alſo manye theim frowarde mynde peruerſe wyll deſpyte ryche men verye gladde wyth ſame theyr myſeryes maximinusthe ſacrileges maximinus hadde thus broughte vnto extreme pouertye famylies many noble famouſe menne reckenynge theim value tryfles towardes ſatyſfienge hys outragiouſe coueteouſnes tourned hys mynde vnto robberye ſpoylynge common treaſorye ſo euer money hadde bene layde vp common prouyſyon corne ſo euer ryches remayned dyſtributed amonges people wyth ſuche treaſoure ſerued deckynge theater gorgiouſe ſettynge furthe feſtyuall pompes playes ſame euerye iote adiudged hymſelfe beſydes gyftes temple statue honour goddes famouſe men wyth ſo euer publycke worke ciuyll ornamentes matter whyche ſeamed conuenyente make money put fyre whiche thing dyd chieflye gnawe vexe harte people cauſed commō mourning ſaying wythoute warre battayle cytye lyke aſſaulted taken ſo many people auentured reſyſte hym defende temple wyſhynge rather ſlayne thaultars immortall goddes ſee theyr coū trey deſtroyedrebelliōs bytter curſes againſte maximinus hereby chiefly myndes commō people beginne grudge againſt thrughoute cytyes thempyre neyther souldiours thē ſelues glad theyr neyghbours kynſfolke rebuked imputed theyr faulte maximinus dyd thus behaue hym ſelfe thieſe enormityes therefore beynge ſmall importaunce dyd prouoke people hatred rebelliō hithervnto thei medled ſaue onely wyth wordes callynge vppon goddes whome maximinus offended none durſte take vppon hym reuenge cauſe vntyll three yeres eande hys reygne vppon lyghte occaſyon affayres tyrrauntes waueringe ſubiecte chaūge affricans fyrſte enterpryſed fall armes rebellyonthe gouernour affriane cauſe certaine liuetenaunt carthage wanted nothynge appartayned extreme furye outeragiouſe tyrranny ſame crepte prince fauour condepning men extorting monei maximinꝰ loued thē moſt al whō knew ſecte factiō yt whoſoeuer therfore charge thēperors treaſour whether thei good mē ſealdome happened depoſed frō office elles feared wt preſent peryll beynge ſkylfull hys vnſatiable auarice dyd althoughe vnwillingly folow accōpany ye reſt thys aforenamed liuetenaunte affryca hauynge violentlye commytted manye greate enormity dyd alſo compaſſe exacte money furthwyth certayne noble ryche yonge men whome fraude circumuented wyth condempnation depryue thē theyr patrimonye ryches theyr aunceſtours left thynge yonge men beynge incenſed dyd deade promyſe paye ſame demaundynge three dayes reſpyte payment meane whyle conſpyrynge togethers manye alreadye ſuffered feared hereafter ſuffer affliction commaunded yonge men theyr ſeruauntes come theyr vyllages farmes clubbes ax vnto executynge theyr maiſters commaundementes came together daye lyghte cytye hydynge vnder theyr garmentes ſuch weapon ſodayne tumulte gotten aſſembled wonderfull greate number men affrica beynge ſelfe greatlye replenyſhed wyth people tyme manye labourer huſbande men alſo daye appeared yonge men commaunded theyr ſeruauntes wayte neare vpon thoughe ſome towne people ſhewe theyr weapon begynne anye violence vntyl ſawe menne armes elles common people aſſaulte theym reuenge facte whyche woulde ſhortlye commyttethe gouernour affrik ſlayne theym ſelues hydynge theyr dagger theyr boſomes went liuetenauntes houſe faynynge woulde ſpeake wyth hym touchynge payment money furthwyth ſodeynlye ſlewe hym ſuſpected ſuche caſualtye hys souldyours drewe furthe theyr ſwordes endeuoured reuenge murder huſbandemen laborer ranne immediatlye byckerynge ſtoutly foughte maiſters eaſelye conſtrayned theyr enemyes turne backes flea whē ye enterpriſe wiſe atchiued ye yong mē hauing ſo deſperatly ſet vpō ye matter rekened one helpe remaine thei heaped vpō late cōmitted miſchiuous act heinous offēce wherfore thei determined aſſociat peryl vnto gouernour prouince induce ye mindes people vnto rebelliō yt whiche thei knew wiſhed thē al ye hatred maximinus yet prohibited frō feare wherefore deape night thei went wt ye multitude proconſuls houſe ſame gordianus obtained ye office whē iiii ſcore yeres old gouernour many prouynces approued ſundry weyghty affaire therefore thei thought would without difficultie take ye rule thempyre vpō ye fynall eande former dignity ſhoulde prince gratefull vnto ye senate people rome beſides noblenes byrth diuers honor ſteppesgordianus choſen emperoure yōge mē aſcended vnto regyment thempyre happened yt ſame day theſe thinges gordianus remained within hys owne houſe hauing defferred buſynes vntill another time ſuſpended adminiſtratiō thynges yonge men wyth ſwordes accōpanied wt great number people repulſed porter entred wt force houſe foūd reſting ſelf vpō bed thei thrōged old mā clothed wt purple ſaluted wt imperiall honor beinge aſtonied wt ſodayn chaūce ſuppoſing deceite wrought purpoſe againſt let ſelfe fall groūd frō bed beſeching thē haue cōpaſſiō vpō old mā whiche neuer offended thē obſerue theyr trueth allegiaunce towards prince while thei thus perſeuered holding ſwordes theyr handes while gordianus partlye throughe feare partly ignoraūce knewe matter ment cauſe ſo ſodayne fortune one yongmen whiche excelled reſte nobilitie eloquēce hauing cōmaūded thē vnto ſilēce holdyng ſword hyltes ſpake ſort twoo peryls yt thone preſentthe wordes one ye yong vnto gordiā manifeſt thother doubtful vncerten eand thou muſt day choſe one either preſerue v thy ſelf cōceaue good hope already haue el without delay ſuffer death hand thou choſe better thē many occaſions good hope thou ſhalt rid waye maximinus worlde abhorred peſtiferous plague cruell tyrannye adde vnto thy life whiche thou haſt hitherunto vertuouſly led famous glory renowne obtayninge senate people rome eternal honour perpetual praiſe thou reiect deny conſpire v wyll hand put death ſelues alſo yf neade wyll accompany diyng haue enterpriſed greater matter ſafe without deſperation miniſter tyrannye dead hath receaued condigne punyſhement hys cruelty beinge lytle earſte ſlayne wyth oure handes wherefore yf thou wylte conſent wyth v become partaker oure perylles thy ſelfe ſhalte obtayne empyre faulte whyche haue committed ſhall reputed worthye prayſe punyſhemente whyles younge man ſpake theyſe wordes reſte multytude beynge vnpacient ſtaye tariynge ſeynge cytyzyns whyche hearde matter aſſembled together wyth one accorde pronounced gordianus emperour albeit refuſed itgordianus ſaluted emperoure excuſed hym ſelfe hys age yet beynge nature ambitious deſyrous glorye dyd wythoute reſiſtence take honoure vppon hym myndynge rather enter daunger come peril preſent beſides thoughte good refuſe ſeynge age come perfection caſe ſo required dye emperoure rome wherfore incōtinently thys al affrique began rebell manye cytyes pulled downe honor maximinus erected image gordyanus hym named theym ſelues affrican thoſe whyche inhabite northe coſte lybyalibia affrikes called romayne tonge aphryques gordianus hauynge ſoiourned v dayes tyſdrumtiſdrum whyche cytye theſe thynges done poſſeſſynge name apparell emperour remoued vnto carthagecarthage ryches bygneſſe carthage alexandrie ſame cytye beynge verye great muche frequented thynges myghte ordered rome carthage haboundaunce rycheſſe reſorte people greatneſſe compaſſe geuynge onelye preheminence rome dooth contende wyth alexandrie egypte ſeconde place thyther folowed gordyanus pryncypall pompe wyth souldyours thoſe partyes cytye yonge men tall comely ſtature like ſimilytude vnto rome whyche garde emperours perſon laurell roddes theyr handes whereby prynces diſcerned priuate perſonnes fyre alſo accordynge vſage caryed hym ſo carthage ſmall ſpace dyd repreſente forme fortune rome thence gordianus ſent manye letter vnto euerye magyſtrate rome noble men senate amonges whome verye manye hys frendes alyes wrote beſydes vnto whole senate people rome ſygnifiyng vnto fauour affrycans towardes hym therwithall accuſing crueltye maximinus whyche perceaued deteſted al men hym ſelfe vſed al gentlenes affabilitye punyſhed wyth exyle vntrewe promoter accuſers vnto theym whyche vnryghteouſly therefore condempned gaue free lybertye defende theyr owne yea reſtored thoſe whyche tofore banyſhed theyr natyue countreyes agayne promyſed geue souldiours rewardes dyſtribute amonges people gyftes man done brought paſſe alſo vytalianvitalianus ye lord greate maiſter maximinus houſeholde mā outragiouſe cruell moſte deare welbeloued maximinus ſlayne within cytie ſelfe rome ſuſpecting man reſyſting hys enterpryſes would feare cauſe alſo turne hym ſente lyuetenaūt prouince ſtoute yonge mā ſtronge body flouryſſhynge age ready attempte peryll hys ſake certayne capitaynes dyuerſe souldiours hys company vnto whome delyuered letter ſealed wyth two seales themperours vſed ſygnifye priuye coūſelles affayres thoſe commaunded entre cytye daye lyghte whyles vytalian buſyed hys accuſtomed affayres go vnto chamber wonte enquyre ſecret thinges appertayned ſafegard hys prince ſhewynge hym thei ſecrete letter vnto maximinus woulde ſet parte commune thinges belonging prince perſon declaring vnto emperours mynde whyles occupied loking vpon seales thei ſhuld murder hym wyth dagger hydde boſomes purpoſe whych enterpryſe atchyued wyſhed dauning daye accuſtomed come furthe thei foūde vitalianus almoſte alone wt fewe onely ſtandinge aboute becauſe ſome nat yet come vnto ſome ſalutaciō done departed day light wherefore finding leyſure fewe ſtanding chāber dore thei declared thoſe thinges ſpake thei eaſely let hauīg deliuered letter while diligently regarded ſygnettes thereofthe deathe vitalianus drewe dagger ſlew departed chamber dagger naked handes euery man giuing place way paſſe thei ſuppoſed bene done maxminus commaundement wont often tymes ſo whome lytle moſt entierly loued thei goyng ſtreate hight sacia via ſhewed furthe epyſtle gordian vnto people delyuered letter hym vnto counſulles thē ſelues magiſtrates rome ſpreading rumor abroad maximyne already ſlayne thing one divulged immediatly al people ranne thrugh ſtreates frō one place lyke men dyſtracte right ſenſes cōmon peoplethe vnconſtācy romayne people euery place vnconſtaūte prone newe chaunges ſo romaine people chiefly wauering vnſtedfaſte beyng knytte greate dyuerſe multitude ſtraungers ¶then image maxymyne reſte honour furthwith pulled downe hatred againſte hym throughe feare hydden thei free lybertie goten man prohibyting powre ſpytte oute senate alſo beyng often aſſembled albeyt certayne reporte maximinus eſtate yet coniecturing preſent fortune rumour true abolyſhe honour pronounced gordianus sonne emperours gordianus son pronounced emperoursimmediatly done promoter eyther fledde away elles ſlayne thoſe thei offēded solliciters beſydes maximine ſuche ſate iudgemente minyſtring tirranny common people drawen throughe ſtreates throwen common ſynkes citye vprore many innocentes ſlayne euery leude perſō entered violentlye houſe hys creditor aduerſarye lawe whome vpon neuer ſo lyghte occaſiō hated ther diſpoiled hys goodes murdered thus vnder coloure lyberty pretence peace deades cyuil warre cōmytted ſo ſlayne dinte clubbe sabinus lyuetenaunte cityesabinus ſlayne whiche endeuoured appeaſe buſye tumulte thieſe thinges dyd people senatours hadde one entered thys peryl thei dyd throughe feare maximine ſollycite thei coulde prouinces rebellyone wherfore ther ambaſſadors choſen chiefeſt order senatours knyghtes whiche ſente vnto gouernours prince letter wherein length declared mynde senate people rome exhorted ſayde ruler haue ſpecyal regarde natiue countrey defendethe coorte rome perſwade nacions vnder continewe allegiaunce towardes romayne people whoſe dominion ouer auncient bonde amitie progenitours longe agone ordeyned many thoſe gouernors receaued ambaſſadors greately enduced people reuolte eaſely brought paſſe ſo greate hatred maximinus wyth euery man thei therefore hauing oute hande ſlayne ſuche magiſtrates amonges maximines parte togither turne vnto romaynes yet fewe ruler either flew ambaſſadors yt cam vnto elles ſent vnder ſure cuſtody vnto maximyne mooſt cruel tormentes dyd put deathe mynde wyll citye rome whyche hurley burley beynge reported vnto maximinus althoughe ſorowfull wythall yet dyd ſayne vtterly contempned fyrſt ſeconde daye remayned quiete wythin hys owne houſe conſultinge wyth hys ſecrete friendes aboute ſame mater althoughe hole armye people regyon knewe vnderſtode thys buſyneſſe prone alſo reuolte ſturred boldenes noueltye ſo greate enterpryſes yet dyd euery man holde peace taking vpon ignoraūt caſe ſo greatly maximinus feared amonges thē nothing hidden hym dyd onely herke vnto euery man wordes alſo watch prye vpon geſture face handes thyrde daye cauſed souldiours aſſemble playne city ſelfe ſytting highe throne reherſed oute booke oration frendes compoſed penned thus oracion maximinusi know verily ſhal declare vnto thing ſtraunge incredible ſelfe ſuppoſe worthy ſo muche wonder laughter thei germaynes ſo often vanquyſſhed moue warre againſt valiaūtnes neyther sarmatyanssarmatians whiche dayly treate wyth v peace perſyās alſo one waſted meſapotamia dothe nowe waxe wyſe quietinge theim ſelues wythin owne houſesmeſapotamye beynge taughte partely wyth youre valiaunte prowes warrefare partely enpriſes whiche haue atchiued wherewith thei became aquaynted gouernaunce armye paſſage ouer ryuers leſte ſhould deteyne thyng woorthye laughter carthaginenſes become madde wyth infortunate olde man doteth throughe extremitye age doute whether perſwaded compelled therunto thei ſtage enterlude play take principalytie vpon armie thei truſte sergauntes talke wyth manye ſkornefull reproches whole cytye senate rome threatenynge wyth geſture hys handes wyth terrible countenaunce menacynge though preſet proclaymed voyage towardes italy hauinge geuen vnto souldyours much monei ſoiourned ther one dai paſſed entred iourney leadynge wyth meruaylous great armye romaine power folowed hym alſo great number germaynes neglected whome eyther force ſubdued el aſſociated amitie vnto hym caryed beſides diuers engens inſtrumentes warre thynges whiche prepared againſt barbarous nacions marche ſlowelye becauſe wagon neceſſaries warre whiche caryed hys whome great confidence whiche alſo fyrſte ſaluted emperour willyngly attempted perylles hys ſaufegarde theyſe commaunded ſet forwarde reſte hoſte enter italye whyles maximinus thus hys iourney affaire people rome yet neglecte title fame italy ſo long tyme preſerued inuaſions forreyne enemyes geue credit vnto falſe periured trayterous tyraunte beynge allured wyth gentle fayned talke runne headlonge vnto theyr owne manifeſt deſtructiō truſt fortune ye warre whyche moſt commonly ſo vncertayne ſometymes greate huge hoſte ſmall number diſcomfited thoſe whych ſeame mightier theym whiche compted weaker diuers tymes vanquiſhed neyther ſhould feare greatneſſe hys armye quod fyghte another mannes quarell ſee good happe victorye ſhall departe another doo fayntlye endure battayle perceauynge ambaſſadours departe maximinus againe wythout anye thyng concluded reported criſpinus hartened abide fortune ye battayle anſwere southſayerssouthſayers whiche reported inwards beaſtes betokened luckye worſhyppe interpretyng apollo whoſe image certaine maximinus owne souldiours affyrmed ſawe ayre fightyng citie thing whether many beleued trueth whether fable pleaſed thē mittigate thereby infamy ſo great army becauſe thei vnequal battayle ſo ſmall number cytezyns exerciſed warres might ſeame ouercome rather ye goddes men certayn ſtraūgenes matter made ſeame credible amdaſſadours retourned wtout reſolute cōcluſion maximinus ſtyrred wt much fury made greater haſt dyd came vnto ryuer whyche runneth xii mile cytye found depe breade channell ſeaſon yeare snowe longe wynter cauſed endure beyng molten vpon next hylles made ſo great floude armye coulde paſſe ouer anye meanes aquileians broken caryed away bridge goodly ſumptuous peace worke buylded auncyent emperours ſquare ſtone many ſmall pillers ſtanding one another vpon ſame wwherfore tharmie coulde paſſe ouer neyther bridge veſſell none nigh hand ſtode ſtyl dumpe muſyng certayne germaynes ignoraunt wyth ſwyftnes violence ryuers italye runne ſuppoſing theyr courſe gentle flow ouer field riuers theyr countrey haue ſwift ſtreame eaſlye congeled ouer wyth iſe aduentured ſelues horſes perfect ſwimming middes chānell throughe vyolence streame drowned maximinus lyen ſtyll campe ii iii dayes caſt depe trenche aboute ſame enemy ſhoulde ſodeynly ſet vpon remayned vpon ſide riuer conſulting howe myght make bridge paſſe ouer whyles ſo abode penſife becauſe tymber boates whiche ioyned together myghte make bridge certayne carpenter declared vnto hym vyllages rounde aboute forſaken inhabitauntes many round tubbes hoggeſheades wherin people wonte cary wyne beinge rounde like ſhyppes yf bounde togethers maner ſmall boates would eaſly carye ouer faſtened togethers couered oziars twigges well baleſſed earth would neuer drowned yt finiſhed ye ſouldiours eaſlye paſſed ouer thother ſhore hauing burned al ye vyllages founde abandoned thin habitaūtes cut ye vine tree wherby greatly defaced ye beauty ye region countrey ſeamed cōpaſſed aboute maner theater wt tree ſet due order vynes ioyned together lyfted vp height like vnto scaffold al plucked ye rootes tharmie approched nigh vnto ye citie neuertheles becauſe wery thēperour would yt ſhould furthwt begyn ye aſſault hauing encāped arrowes ſhoote frō citie deuided thē hundred appoynted order marching like vnto wedge ſmal broade behinde limitting euery company part wall ſcale batter gaue lycence recreate ſelues one daye paſſed began geue aſſault hauing moued wall ſortes engyns kynd batterie omitted almoſt euery day cruell ſkyrmyſhes fought souldyours enuironed walles toyle nette fought muche ſtoutnes ſtomacke contrarye parte aquileiens reſyſted verye valiauntlye hauynge ſhutte dores temple houſes dyd together wyth theyr wyues child vpon walles tower batylmentes defende theyr cytye neyther age whiche refuſed fyghte countrey maximinus pulled downe al suburbes whatſoeuer buyldynge without cytye tymber wherof made kynde engyns inſtrumentes wherwith might batter walles leaſt wyſe ſome part therof whereby armye myght enter ye cytye ſpoylyng ſackyng defacynge ſame leaue deſolate voyde habitation thoughte yt woulde againſt honour go vnto rome deſtroyed cytye fyrſt reſiſted italy wherefore rode wyth hys sonne whome ioyned vnto hym empyre amonges souldyours promyſyng many good morowes exhortynge theym ſtande lyke menne theyr tacklynge cytezyns aquileia threw downe great ſtones vpon hauing fylled verye many ladels brimſtonea ſore repulſe lyme pitche ſoone souldyours began ſcale wals powred downe ye ſame ſo ſaue ſeamed violent ſhowres whē ye pitche baggage fell vpō ye naked partes ye ſouldiours body thei threw frō thē brigāders reſt harneſſe ye yron wexing hoate timber engyns ſet fyre mā mighte ſee souldiours throwe away owne harneſſe thing hauīg colour thei diſpoyled vanquiſſhers inuented rather ſubtlitie arte force batayle whereby happened many souldiours eyther loſte theyr ſyghte elles face bare partes body burned aquileyēs threw downe alſo towres engins woode many torche ſtraues couered wyth roſen pitch whoſe endes ſharpened heades lyke vnto arowes whyche beyng kindeled ſticked faſte timber worke dyd eaſely ſet fyre notwithſtanding fyrſte day fortune equall eyther ſyde anon courage maximinus armye dyd aſwage becauſe theyr hope fruſtrate deceiued thē thei wexed euery day peſife thoſe thei ſuppoſed wold abyd brunt firſt theyr force thei nowe perceiued onely ſhrincke alſo reſyſte valeaūtely contrariwyſe ſtomackes aquilenſes daylye enhaunſed hauinge thrugh vſe obtayned bothe thexperte feate fyghtinge therwithall manfull corage thei ſo deſpyſed souldiours mocked ieſtyng maximinus came nighe vnto walles bluſtering oute many opprobrious taūtes againſt sone wherewith chaufed could auenge ſelfe vppon hys enemyes put cruel death many capitaines alleging yt thei like valeaunte men true ſubiectes done full endeuour aſſaultinge citye wherby came paſſe souldiours came angry towardes hym enemyes contempt deriſion chaunſed beſydes aquileyens aboūded plenty vitayle neceſſaries ſo euer expedient ſuſtenaunce men horſes ſame hande brought citye thother ſyde armye languiſhed penury foode tree cut downe fieldes waſted ſome souldiours lay cabbans ſuch thei could haſte make ſom open fieldes ſubiect heate sonne weatenes rayne neyther anye kynde noryſhmente broughte vnto theim ſelues cattell wayes paſſages diligence romaine ſhut vp greate walles gate senate alſo ſente certayne senatours companie armed perſonnes choſen oute italye defende shore hauens geuing man licēce ſayle thinges done rome kept cloſe eares maximine highe wayes beſydes bypathes diligently watched man ſhould paſſe came paſſe armye whiche beſyeged towne ſelfe alſo encloſed rounde aboute thei coulde neyther take aquileia paſſe forward towards rome wante ſhyppes wagon whiche hande taken vp romaine rumor alſo thrughe ſuſpicion augmented romayne people already armes italy illyrian barbarous naciōs whiche enhabyte eaſte southe contreys wyth one conſent conſpyred ioyne together againſt maximinus deſpyte grudge bare vnto hym wherefore souldiours fell diſpayre good hope beyng afflicted wyth ſcarcetye thinges hauyng water ſuch thei drew ye ryuer defiled bloode deade carcaſes aquileyens threwe ryuer ſuch deade body thei coulde bury thoſe whyche periſhed ſworde ſicknes campe throwen ryuer lykewyſe amonges whome many whyche died famin hauing thei drowned ſome breath remaynynge whyles army aboade thus ſorowfull voyde ſuccoure ſodeinly maximinus reſted hys pauilion one daye vacant batayle souldiours gone reſte theim ſelues theyr cabans tentes men armes theyr stacions within citye rome vnder hyll alban therin wiues childrē cō ſulted agreed ſlea maximyne thei might one exempt longe inexplicable ſyege cytye mouing warre againſt italy loue tiraunt abhorred men wherefore taking corage vnto nonetyde thei wente pauilion yeoman hys garde cōſpiring together thei hadde pulled downe hys image thei ſlewe hym hys sonne came furthethe deth maximinus son ſpeke vnto souldiours lord great maiſter houſe deareſt frēdes threw body furth wt deſpite leuyng deuoured dogges byrdes ſēding onely two emperours heades vnto rome eande lyfe maximinus son receyuinge condigne punyſhmente yll ordered gouernaunce firſt tidinges two prynces death army ſtode ſtyll amaſed vncertayne thei might doo equally acceptable vnto eſpeciallye vnto panonians barbarous thracian hadde delyuered empyre vnto maximinus perceiued deade coulde vndone helde ſelues contented althoughe vnwillingly fayned reioyce reſte layeng ſyde weapon thei went walles aquileye lyke peaceable mē declaring death maximyne deſyred gate might ſet opē vnto beyng nowe mortall enemyes become louing frendes capitaynes aquileia would permyt ſhewed furth vppon walles image maximus albinus gordian emperours crowned garlandes lawrell vnto image ſelues fyrſte making ioyful acclamacions exorted army alſo acknowledge reuerence whome senate people rome hadde choſen emperours ſaid thei gordians paſſed amonges goddes ſet furth alſo vpon walles market neceſſaries greate abundaunce meate wyne garmētes thinges riche floriſhing cytie could miniſter vnto thing meruelouſly abaſhe souldiours perceyued cytezins ſtore ynoughe vitayll abyde farre longer ſeage ſide ſelues afflicted wante foode ſhould rather haue peryſſhed conquered citie abounding wyth thinges expedient man relief whyles souldiours thus aboade vnder walles tooke ſuch thinges neceſſitie required companye citezins countenaunce peace frendſhip forme ſiege yet remaining romayne souldiours laye aboute walles whiche encloſed ſhut meane theiſe thinges aquileya ye horſe men caried emperours heades rome making great haſte ſpedy diligence receiued euery citie town gate opē multitude citezins enhabitauntes berynge lawrell handes hauinge paſſed ye mariſhes lake whiche betwene altinumaltinum rauenna maximꝰ rauenna thei founde maximus rauenna leuieng waging souldiours citye italy calling great number germains vnto ayde ſent cōmon people germany whō proconſulſhip amonges prudentely gouerned while thus muſtering power againſt maximine ye horſemē arriued thīges ſo ſodēly wt expectaciō reported furthwt people ran vnto aulters ſacrifice euery man ſingyng reioyſynge victory whiche wythoute troubleſome buſynes obtayned maximus ſacryfyce eanded diſmiſſed horſmen rome cary thither ſayd heades declare whole circumſtaūce vnto people ariued cytye hauynge putte heades vpon twoo speares caried ſame throughe ye ſtreates ſeane people tonge tell ioye myrth daye perſon eyther yonge olde ranne vnto temple aulters man abode within hys owne houſe ranne lyke madde men ſhoutynge reioyſynge one gatherynge theym ſelues together circle thoughe ſome manne woulde make oration vnto albinus hym ſelfe offered hundreth beaſtes magiſtrates reioyſed aboue meaſure though eſcaped ye axe whych henge ouer theyr neckes purſeuaūtes poſtes ſente beſydes wyth laurell theyr handes beare thoſe newes vnto prouinces whyle thys ſo great ioye myrthe continued amonges romaynes maximus remoued frō rauenna went vnto aquileia hauyng paſſed al maryſhes whyche ryuer eridanus nyghe lake doth ouerflowe ſo runne sea vii armes therefore nyghe enhabitauntes cal ſame lake theyr tonge vii sea furthwith aquileiens opened gate receaued maximus verye manye cytyes italye ſente theyr chiefe magiſtrates ambaſſadors vnto clothed white garmētes crowned wyth laurell bringinge theym image theyr countrey goddes crownes golde yf amonges chiefeſt iewels wher withall gratified maximus ſtrowed bowes paſſage armye beſieged aquileia mette hym alſo peaceable apparell wyth laurell handes ſo trewe louyng affection fayned good wyll reuerence tyme onelye applyed vnto preſente ſtate prince yea many morned priuelye choſen ſlayne thoſe whyche senate created poſſeſſed principalytie maximus ſpente firſt ſecond daye offering ſacrifice thyrd day aſſembled al ye army together playne ſitting ye tribunal ſeate made thys oration vnto howe profitable penitence fauour reconciled wyth romayne people hathe vnto ſelues haue experience throughlye learned acceptyng peace warre obſeruyng byrth actes done certayne degree aſcended senate people rome haue elected neyther poſſeſſion principalitie peculier vnto one man olde antiquitie common vnto romayn people cytye ſelfe eſtablyſhed fortune thempyre v wyth commytted adminiſtration ſame wyl therfore retaine wyth order modeſtye becommeth geue due honour reuerence vnto prynces ye ſhall onely obtayne vnto ſelues bleſſed lyfe flowyng countreyes beynge oure charge ſee barbarous people remayne peace defende ſame whyles two emperours bothe citye forreyne affaire ſhalbe adminiſtred eaſlye one theym beynge alwayes readye go whyther notwithſtanding empire gouerned bothe openly priuely much modeſt grauitie euerye man ſpake well people gladde wyth prynces noble men borne worthye thempyre yet ſpytful crabbed ſtomackes pretorian
